❯ Read @KNOWN-ISSUES.md                                                         
  ⎿  Read KNOWN-ISSUES.md (128 lines)

● Read done. Summary:

  4 bugs (all likely inherited from upstream microfuzz):
  1. Punctuation not word boundary — comma demote strong multi-word match to
  junk tier. Highest impact.
  2. Boundary-contains tier check only first indexOf occurrence — later boundary
  occurrence missed.
  3. Highlight ranges point into wrong word — same indexOf habit in matches.
  4. Multi-word tier score 1.5 + words * 0.2 — more query words = worse rank.

  Hazard: smart fuzzy over long text match almost anything. Doc fix: scope
  smart/aggressive to short labels, strategy: "off" for documents. Plus
  stable-sort ordering guarantee worth documenting.

  5 feature requests: per-field strategy/weight, per-field scores, generic
  FuzzySearchOptions<T>, exported tier constants, match-density signal for fuzzy
  tier.

  Repros pinned in test/known-issues.test.ts — passing tests = current behavior,
  it.fails = desired. What next — fix bugs, check upstream, or something else?

✻ Baked for 7s

     /plan to edit
     mikrofuzz test suite

     Context

     The library has exactly one test file — test/known-issues.test.ts, a
     regression tracker for 4 known bugs (its convention: passing it pins
     current buggy behaviour, it.fails pins desired behaviour and flips to
     "unexpected pass" when a fix lands). Nothing else is tested:
     createFuzzySearch (key/getText/strategies/sort), normalizeText, the
     aggressive strategy, the scoring tiers, and range semantics have zero
     coverage. pnpm lint:types (tsc --noEmit) excludes test/, so test files
     aren't even type-checked.

     Goal: a comprehensive main suite covering the full public API that passes
     now and still passes after bugs 1–4 are fixed (pinning buggy behaviour is
     known-issues' job, not the main suite's). Plus: type-check test/, add 2
     newly discovered warts to KNOWN-ISSUES.md with tracker tests, fix one wrong
     README comment. No CI changes (user deselected).

     All expected scores below were hand-verified against src/index.ts (tier
     ladder matchesFuzzily lines 132–177, scoreConsecutiveLetters 38–54,
     smartFuzzyMatch 86–130, aggressiveFuzzyMatch 56–84).

     Files

     test/known-issues.test.ts        # existing — only append warts 5–6 (see
     §5)
     test/normalize.test.ts           # new
     test/fuzzy-match.test.ts         # new
     test/strategies.test.ts          # new
     test/create-fuzzy-search.test.ts # new
     tsconfig.json                    # include test/, drop rootDir
     README.md                        # fix line 43 score comment
     KNOWN-ISSUES.md                  # append bugs 5–6

     Conventions (match known-issues.test.ts): tabs, import { describe, expect, 
     it } from "vitest", import from ../src/index. toBe for tier literals (0,
     0.1, 0.5, 0.9, 1, 2 — literal constants in source); toBeCloseTo for
     computed sums (fuzzy tier).

     Fix-resilience rules (critical)

     Bugs 1–4 will be fixed; the main suite must survive the fixes:

     - Bug 1 (punctuation → word boundary): no punctuation adjacent to matched
     words in test inputs. Existing boundary chars (space, -, –, (, quotes) are
     safe — the fix only adds characters.
     - Bug 2 (only first indexOf occurrence boundary-checked): in every
     contains-tier input, the FIRST occurrence of the query must be the deciding
     one, and tier-2 inputs must have NO boundary occurrence anywhere (e.g.
     "concatenate"/"cat" safe; "concatenate the cat" is known-issues territory).
     - Bug 3 (ranges in wrong word): assert exact ranges only where the matched
     substring occurs exactly once, at the asserted position.
     - Bug 4 (multi-word 1.5 + n*0.2): NEVER assert exact multi-word scores.
     Assert band > 1 && < 2, and only with 2-word queries — both suggested fixes
     (flat 1.5; subtract per word) keep a 2-word match inside (1, 2), but a
     3-word subtract-fix could dip to ≤ 1. Exact 1.9 pin lives in known-issues.

     Test inventory

     test/normalize.test.ts

     describe("normalizeText") — it.each table: ["HELLO","hello"],
     ["Café","cafe"], ["Über","uber"], ["jalapeño","jalapeno"], ["Łódź","lodz"]
     (ł has no NFD decomposition — exercises the regexŁ path), ["Zażółć gęślą 
     jaźń","zazolc gesla jazn"], ["  padded  ","padded"], ["MiXeD CaSe","mixed 
     case"], ["",""]. Plus: punctuation untouched ("a.b,c:d;e/f" unchanged),
     internal whitespace preserved ("a  b"), idempotence loop over table
     (normalizeText(normalizeText(x)) === normalizeText(x)).

     test/fuzzy-match.test.ts

     - Result shape: fuzzyMatch("banana","ban") → { item: "banana", score: 0.5, 
     matches: [[[0,2]]] } (item is ORIGINAL text); fuzzyMatch("cherry","xyz") →
     null.
     - Tier 0/0.1: ("Apple","Apple") → 0, matches [[[0,4]]]; ("Apple","apple") →
     0.1; ("apple","APPLE") → 0.1; ("Café","cafe") → 0.1; ("Łódź","lodz") →
     0.1.
     - Tier 0.5 prefix: ("banana","ban") → 0.5 [[0,2]];
     case/diacritic-insensitive ("Banana","bAN") → 0.5.
     - Tier 0.9/1 boundary contains: ("Hello World","World") → 0.9 [[6,10]];
     ("Hello World","world") → 1 [[6,10]]; ("Hello World","wor") → 1 [[6,8]]
     (README example). it.each existing boundary chars: ("well-known","known") →
     0.9 [[5,9]]; ("foo (bar)","bar") → 0.9 [[5,7]]; ("2019–2024","2024") → 0.9
     [[5,8]]. First occurrence is the boundary one in every input.
     - Multi-word tier [band only, 2-word queries — bug-4 rule]: ("the quick 
     brown fox","fox quick") → score > 1 && < 2; ranges [[[4,8],[16,18]]] (each
     word occurs once, sorted ascending). Negative: ("foxglove quickly","fox 
     quick") — itemWords lack both → falls to smart fuzzy, assert score > 2 only
     (verified: matches via " qu" 3-char chunk, actual 3.2 — but band only,
     chunk math fragile).
     - Tier 2 contains-anywhere (no boundary occurrence anywhere in input):
     ("concatenate","cat") → 2 [[3,5]]; ("tsunami","sun") → 2 [[1,3]];
     ("banana","nan") → 2 [[2,4]].
     - Edge cases: ("","a") → null; ("cat","catalog") → null; ("cherry","xyz") →
     null. Do NOT test fuzzyMatch(text,"") here — that's wart 5 (known-issues).
     - Range semantics: inclusive proof — r = fuzzyMatch("Hello World","wor");
     "Hello World".slice(start, end+1) === "Wor". Fuzzy ranges
     ascending/non-overlapping via ("big cat","bigcat") → [[0,2],[4,6]].
     - Cross-API consistency: loop corpus [["banana","ban"],["Hello 
     World","wor"],["concatenate","cat"],["big cat","bigcat"],["cherry","xyz"]]
     — createFuzzySearch([t])(q)[0]?.score equals fuzzyMatch(t,q)?.score ?? 
     undefined.
     - Tier monotonicity: "banana" with queries ["banana","BANANA","ban","nan"]
     → scores [0, 0.1, 0.5, 2] strictly ascending; "Hello World" with ["Hello 
     World","hello world","World","world"] → [0, 0.1, 0.9, 1].

     test/strategies.test.ts

     All via createFuzzySearch (fuzzyMatch hardcodes smart). Fuzzy scores
     verified by hand-trace:

     - Smart (default): ["hello world"], ("hewo") → toBeCloseTo(2.8), matches
     [[[0,1],[6,7]]] (two word-start chunks, +0.4 each). Mid-word 3+ chunk:
     ["xylophone tuner"], ("phonetun") → toBeCloseTo(3.2), [[[4,8],[10,12]]]
     (len-5 mid-word +0.8, word-start +0.4). Rejects short mid-word chunks:
     ["abcdef"], ("adf") → [].
     - Aggressive: ["abcdef"], {strategy:"aggressive"}, ("adf") →
     toBeCloseTo(5.6), [[[0,0],[3,3],[5,5]]] (+0.4, +1.6, +1.6). Agrees with
     smart on boundary-aligned input: ["hello world"], ("hewo") → 2.8.
     - Off: ["big cat"], {strategy:"off"}: ("bigcat") → []; ("big") → 0.5;
     ("cat") → 0.9 (keeps non-fuzzy tiers).
     - Chunk scoring: full-word chunks cheapest — smart ["big cat"], ("bigcat")
     → toBeCloseTo(2.4), [[[0,2],[4,6]]] (two full words, +0.2 each). Word-start
     chunks: ["sad unknown night"], ("sun") → toBeCloseTo(2.8),
     [[[0,0],[4,5]]]. Relational: 2.4 (2 clean chunks) < 5.6 (3 fragmented) —
     documents "fewer chunks = better".

     test/create-fuzzy-search.test.ts

     - String collections: README fruits — ["apple","banana","cherry","grape"],
     ("ban") → exactly [{ item:"banana", score:0.5, matches:[[[0,2]]] }];
     ("xyz") → []; empty collection → [].
     - Empty/whitespace query: (""), ("   "), ("\t") → [] (normalize trims to
     empty).
     - key option: users = [{id:1,name:"John Doe"},{id:2,name:"Jane Smith"}],
     {key:"name"}, ("john") → 1 result, item toBe(users[0]) (reference), score
     0.5 (prefix — README comment says 1, that's the doc bug), matches
     [[[0,3]]]. Missing key skipped without crash: [{name:"apple"},{other:"x"}],
     ("app") → 1 result (text || "" path).
     - getText multi-field (needs as cast — getText takes unknown; relevant once
     test/ is type-checked): matches shape one-entry-per-field with null —
     [{name:"John Doe",email:"john@example.com"}], getText → [name,email],
     ("doe") → score 1, matches [[[5,7]], null] (email has no "d"). Score is MIN
     across fields: [{name:"pineapple",email:"app@x.com"}], ("app") → score
     0.5, matches [[[4,6]],[[0,2]]] (name tier-2 @4 — no boundary "app" in
     "pineapple" → bug-2-safe; email prefix). Null field entries tolerated:
     getText → [u.name, null].
     - Sort order — full ladder in one search, query "green tea" over (no
     punctuation anywhere → bug-1-safe):
     | item                  | tier                                       |
     score       |
     |-----------------------|--------------------------------------------|-----
     --------|
     | "green tea"           | exact                                      | 0
            |
     | "Green Tea"           | normalized exact                           | 0.1
            |
     | "green tea ice cream" | prefix                                     | 0.5
            |
     | "matcha green tea"    | boundary exact-case @7                     | 0.9
            |
     | "iced Green Tea"      | boundary normalized @5                     | 1
            |
     | "tea garden green"    | multi-word (2 words)                       | band
     (1, 2) |
     | "evergreen teapot"    | contains @4 (no boundary occurrence)       | 2
            |
     | "greedy nectar team"  | smart fuzzy (verified matches, actual 3.6) | > 2
            |

     - Assert: items in exactly this order; scores non-decreasing pairwise;
     tier-literal scores with toBe, multi-word/fuzzy as bands.
     - Sort stability: ["banana","bandana"], ("ban") → both 0.5, order
     preserved; reversed input ["bandana","banana"] → reversed output.
     - Unicode: ["Señor García"], ("garcia") → score 1, matches [[[6,11]]];
     ["Łódź"], ("lodz") → 0.1.

     §4 Type-check test/

     tsconfig.json: change "include" to ["src/**/*.ts", "test/**/*.ts"] and
     delete "rootDir": "src" (otherwise tsc errors "not under rootDir"). Emit is
     owned by unbuild (build.config.ts), root tsconfig only serves tsc --noEmit
     + editors — safe. Consequence: getText tests need as casts (types.ts
     declares getText?: (item: unknown) => ...).

     §5 New known-issues entries (bugs 5–6)

     Append to KNOWN-ISSUES.md and test/known-issues.test.ts, following the
     existing convention (passing pins + it.fails desired):

     - Bug 5 — fuzzyMatch(text, "") returns a bogus match. The empty-query guard
     exists only in createFuzzySearch; startsWith("") is always true, so
     fuzzyMatch("abc","") → score 0.5 with degenerate range [[0,-1]]. Pin
     current (score 0.5, range [[0,-1]]); it.fails desired: null (consistent
     with createFuzzySearch's []).
     - Bug 6 — range width uses raw queryLen against normalized-text indices
     (tiers 0.9/1/2, src/index.ts:152,157,172): un-trimmed query " wor "
     over-widens the range; leading-whitespace items shift ranges relative to
     the original string (trim shortens normalized text). Repro to pin:
     fuzzyMatch("Hello World", " wor ") → range [[6,10]] (5 wide for a 3-char
     effective query); desired [[6,8]]. Main suite avoids
     leading/trailing-whitespace inputs in range assertions.

     §6 README fix

     Line 43: // [{ item: { id: 1, name: "John Doe" }, score: 1, matches: [...] 
     }] → score: 0.5 ("john" is a prefix of normalized "john doe").

     Explicitly excluded

     - CI workflow changes (user deselected).
     - fast-check: recommend against — new dev-dep vs zero-dep ethos; scoring is
     a finite deterministic tier ladder where curated tables give equivalent
     coverage. Property-style loops (idempotence, monotonicity, cross-API) use
     plain vitest.
     - No pinning of bug-1–4 behaviour outside known-issues.

     Verification

     1. pnpm install
     2. pnpm lint:types — exits 0; confirm test files checked: npx tsc --noEmit 
     --listFilesOnly | grep test/ lists all 5 test files.
     3. pnpm test — 5 files green. known-issues must report its it.fails tests
     as expected-failures (after §5: 9+2 regular passes + 5+2 expected fails).
     Any "unexpected pass" means a fix landed → known-issues cleanup, not a
     main-suite problem.
     4. Fix-resilience audit: grep -n "toBeCloseTo(1\.9\|toBeCloseTo(2\.1" 
     test/*.test.ts → matches only known-issues.test.ts; no punctuation-glued
     match targets in the 4 new files; no 3+-word multi-word band assertions.
     5. Simulated-fix check (when bug fixes land later): the 4 new files must
     stay green with zero edits; only known-issues.test.ts changes.

       75  **Suggested fix:** flat 1.5, or subtract per word matched. A t

       78 +### 5. `fuzzyMatch` accepts an empty query                    
       79 +                                                              
       80 +The empty-query guard exists only in `createFuzzySearch` (retu
          +rns `[]`).                                                    
       81 +In `fuzzyMatch` the query reaches `normalizedItem.startsWith(n
          +ormalizedQuery)`,                                             
       82 +and `startsWith("")` is always true — so an empty query is rep
          +orted as a                                                    
       83 +prefix match with a degenerate range.                         
       84 +                                                              
       85 +```ts                                                         
       86 +createFuzzySearch(["abc"])(""); // [] — guarded               
       87 +fuzzyMatch("abc", ""); // score 0.5, matches [[[0, -1]]] (!)  
       88 +```                                                           
       89 +                                                              
       90 +**Suggested fix:** early-return `null` from `fuzzyMatch` when 
          +the normalized                                                
       91 +query is empty, matching `createFuzzySearch`.                 
       92 +                                                              
       93 +### 6. Highlight width uses the raw query length              
       94 +                                                              
       95 +Tiers 0.9/1/2 build ranges as `[idx, idx + queryLen - 1]` wher
          +e `queryLen`                                                  
       96 +is `query.length` — the raw, un-normalized query — but `idx` i
          +ndexes the                                                    
       97 +normalized text. Whitespace padding in the query (which `norma
          +lizeText`                                                     
       98 +trims) inflates the width past the actual match.              
       99 +                                                              
      100 +```ts                                                         
      101 +fuzzyMatch("Hello World", "wor").matches;   // [[[6, 8]]]     
      102 +fuzzyMatch("Hello World", " wor ").matches; // [[[6, 10]]] (!)
          + — score still 1                                              
      103 +```                                                           
      104 +                                                              
      105 +Leading whitespace in the *item* shifts ranges the other way, 
          +since the                                                     
      106 +normalized text is shorter than the original the range indexes
          + into.                                                        
      107 +                                                              
      108 +**Suggested fix:** derive the range width from `normalizedQuer
          +yLen`, not the                                                
      109 +raw `queryLen`.

  ⎿  Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/plan-a-test-suite-lovely-wigderson.md · 
     /plan to edit
     mikrofuzz: refactor src/index.ts into concern-separated files + naming 
     audit

     Context

     src/index.ts is 283 lines mixing five concerns: word boundaries, fuzzy
     chunk
     scoring, subsequence strategies, the tier ladder, and the public collection
     API.
     Bugs 1–6 are queued next; splitting first gives each fix a small, focused
     file
     to land in. This is a behavior-preserving reorganization — the test suite
     (77
     pass + 7 expected-fail, importing only fuzzyMatch/createFuzzySearch/
     normalizeText from ../src/index) must stay bit-identical.

     User decisions (this session): balanced granularity (~4 new files, not
     one-per-symbol),
     and the naming audit is documentation only — no identifier renames this
     pass;
     docs/naming.md records the vocabulary and flags inconsistencies for a later
     PR.

     Hard constraint: build.config.ts entry is ./src/index and package.json
     exports . → dist/index.mjs+.d.ts, so src/index.ts must remain and re-export
     exactly today's public surface: fuzzyMatch, createFuzzySearch,
     normalizeText,
     export type * from "./types". No new public symbols. Zero new dependencies.

     Target src/ layout (balanced)

     File: types.ts (unchanged)
     Concern: Type vocabulary
     Symbols moved in: —
     Imports: —
     Exports: all 7 types
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     File: normalize.ts (unchanged)
     Concern: Fold text to canonical form
     Symbols moved in: —
     Imports: —
     Exports: normalizeText
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     File: shared.ts (new, common)
     Concern: Primitives shared across fuzzy + tier concerns
     Symbols moved in: validWordBoundaries, isValidWordBoundary, + named score
     constants (below)
     Imports: none
     Exports: isValidWordBoundary, all score constants (validWordBoundaries
     stays
     module-private)
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     File: fuzzy.ts (new)
     Concern: Subsequence chunk assembly + scoring
     Symbols moved in: scoreConsecutiveLetters, aggressiveFuzzyMatch,
     smartFuzzyMatch
     Imports: isValidWordBoundary + chunk constants from ./shared; type 
     {HighlightRanges} from ./types
     Exports: aggressiveFuzzyMatch, smartFuzzyMatch
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     File: match.ts (new)
     Concern: Tier ladder: rank one field vs query
     Symbols moved in: matchesFuzzily, local sortRangeTuple
     Imports: strategies from ./fuzzy; isValidWordBoundary + tier constants from

     ./shared; type {Range,HighlightRanges,FuzzySearchStrategy} from ./types
     Exports: matchesFuzzily
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     File: search.ts (new)
     Concern: Public API over one string + collections
     Symbols moved in: fuzzyMatch, createFuzzySearch, local MAX_SAFE_INTEGER,
     local
     sortByScore
     Imports: matchesFuzzily from ./match; normalizeText from ./normalize; types
     Exports: fuzzyMatch, createFuzzySearch
     ────────────────────────────────────────
     File: index.ts (shrinks to barrel)
     Concern: Public surface + header docstring
     Symbols moved in: header docstring (lines 1–14) stays
     Imports: re-exports only
     Exports: public: fuzzyMatch,createFuzzySearch from ./search; normalizeText
     from
     ./normalize; export type * from "./types"

     Comparators are single-use → kept local to their one caller (sortRangeTuple
     in
     match.ts, sortByScore in search.ts), per requirement 2's strict reading —
     no
     sort.ts. MAX_SAFE_INTEGER sentinel stays local to search.ts.

     shared.ts — the common file (requirement 2)

     Two things are used by both the fuzzy concern and the tier-ladder concern,
     so
     they move to shared.ts:

     Word boundary — copy the Set literal byte-for-byte (' []()-–—\'"""' — two
     spaces + brackets/parens/hyphen + en/em dash + escaped quote + three
     double-quotes;
     dedup makes the duplicates harmless but the literal must not drift).
     Verified by the
     0.9/1 boundary tests.

     Named score constants — replace inline magic numbers with names (this is
     new
     constants, not identifier renaming, so it's within the doc-only decision,
     and it is
     the clearest instance of "shared vocabulary → common file"):

     // tier scores (used by match.ts)
     SCORE_EXACT            = 0     SCORE_BOUNDARY_EXACT     = 0.9
     SCORE_NORMALIZED_EXACT = 0.1   SCORE_BOUNDARY           = 1
     SCORE_PREFIX           = 0.5   SCORE_MULTI_WORD_BASE    = 1.5
     SCORE_CONTAINS         = 2     SCORE_MULTI_WORD_PER_WORD = 0.2
     // fuzzy chunk scores (used by fuzzy.ts)
     FUZZY_BASE = 2   CHUNK_WHOLE_WORD = 0.2   CHUNK_WORD_START = 0.4
     CHUNK_LONG = 0.8  CHUNK_SCATTERED = 1.6

     Float-identity rules (mandatory): (1) each constant holds the exact source
     literal token; (2) do NOT pre-fold expressions — line 162 stays
     SCORE_MULTI_WORD_BASE + queryWords.length * SCORE_MULTI_WORD_PER_WORD,
     chunk sums
     stay score += CHUNK_* in original order; (3) keep coincidental duplicates
     as
     separate names — 0.2 is both SCORE_MULTI_WORD_PER_WORD and
     CHUNK_WHOLE_WORD;
     2 is both SCORE_CONTAINS and FUZZY_BASE. Do NOT extract the 3 in
     Math.min(3, …) (line 106) here — it's a smart-strategy tuning value, not a
     score;
     leave inline or name SMART_MIN_CHUNK local to fuzzy.ts. Sentinels
     (-1, -2, MAX_SAFE_INTEGER) stay inline.

     Import DAG (acyclic)

     index → search, normalize, types
     search → match, normalize, types
     match → fuzzy, shared, types
     fuzzy → shared, types
     shared, normalize, types → (leaves)
     Levels: L0 {types, normalize, shared} · L1 {fuzzy} · L2 {match} · L3
     {search} · L4
     {index}. Every edge strictly decreases level → no cycles. Guard rule while
     editing:
     never import "upward" (fuzzy↛match, match↛search, nothing↛index).

     docs/naming.md (new — documentation only, no renames)

     Sections: NOUNS table · VERBS table · INCONSISTENCIES · canonical glossary.

     NOUNS to catalog (term — meaning — where): item, element, collection,
     text/texts,
     field, query, queryWords, itemWords/wordSet, match/matches, Range,
     HighlightRanges,
     FuzzyMatches, chunk, indices, score, tier, boundary/word, occurrence,
     strategy,
     result(s), searcher, options, key, getText, preprocessed/processed,
     normalizedItem/
     normalizedText/normalized, queryChar, minQueryChunk, the Idx family (idx,
     itemIdx,
     queryIdx, first/last/chunkFirst/chunkLastIdx, contains/exactContainsIdx),
     the Len
     family (queryLen, normalized*Len, chunkLength, minChunkLen,
     query/itemCharsLeft),
     normalize regexes, MAX_SAFE_INTEGER sentinel.

     VERBS: normalize, match, score, create, search, sort,
     startsWith/contains(indexOf),
     isValidWordBoundary/isStartOfWord/isEndOfWord,
     preprocess/extract(getText·key),
     split/slice, push/every/has/min.

     INCONSISTENCIES (15) — flag each with a recommended canonical name
     (recommendation
     only; not applied this pass):
     - (a) item overloaded: raw field-string (matchesFuzzily) vs collection
     element
     (FuzzyResult.item). → reserve item for the element; field-string sense →
     field.
     - (b) element vs item vs "result item" = one concept, three names →
     canonical item.
     - (c) text vs item both = raw field-string → canonical field (public
     fuzzyMatch(text,…) keeps text as documented alias).
     - (d) Range reused for highlight spans AND chunk index-pairs → add alias
     type Chunk = Range for runs.
     - (e) indices local IS a HighlightRanges → chunks: Chunk[].
     - (f) matchesFuzzily reads as a boolean predicate but returns
     [score,ranges]|null
     → matchField / rankField.
     - (g) firstIdx/lastIdx/chunkFirstIdx/chunkLastIdx vs Range's start/end →
     standardize on start/end.
     - (h) "off" strategy ≠ matching off — only the fuzzy fallback is disabled;
     and
     fuzzyMatch hardcodes "smart" so "off"/"aggressive" are unreachable via it →
     document "strategy governs only the fuzzy fallback tier".
     - (i) Len (abbrev) vs chunkLength (spelled) → standardize on Len.
     - (j) matches double-plural (per-field list of range-lists) → document;
     consider fieldMatches.
     - (k) getText returns Array<string|null> despite singular name → note
     getFields.
     - (l) preprocessed vs processed differ only by prefix → inner processed →
     fields.
     - (m) normalizedItem/normalizedText/normalized = three names →
     normalizedField.
     - (n) queryChar: string can be undefined past query end (relied-on
     coercion) →
     type-honesty note; leave code.
     - (o) sortByScore (by-what) vs sortRangeTuple (of-what) → sortByRangeStart.

     Canonical glossary: item=collection entry (public) · field=one raw
     searchable
     string · normalizedField=its normalized form · chunk(type Chunk=Range)=a
     consecutive matched run · Range=a highlight span · matches=per-field
     highlight
     lists · matchField=rank one field · start/end=bounds ·
     SMART_MIN_CHUNK=smart
     lookahead width.

     Execution order (leaf-first; run pnpm lint:types + pnpm test after EACH 
     step)

     1. shared.ts — move boundary Set (verbatim) + isValidWordBoundary; add
     named
     score constants. Update index.ts to import from it and swap the inline
     literals.
     Gate: boundary tests + all toBe/toBeCloseTo score tests green.
     2. fuzzy.ts — move scoreConsecutiveLetters + both strategy fns; import
     chunk
     constants + isValidWordBoundary from ./shared.
     3. match.ts — move matchesFuzzily + sortRangeTuple; import strategies from
     ./fuzzy, boundary + tier constants from ./shared. Guard: no import of
     ./search.
     4. search.ts — move fuzzyMatch, createFuzzySearch, local sortByScore +
     MAX_SAFE_INTEGER; import matchesFuzzily from ./match, normalizeText.
     5. Shrink index.ts to the barrel — keep header docstring; re-export the
     exact
     public surface. Gate: pnpm build, diff dist/index.d.ts + dist/index.mjs
     exports vs baseline — must be exactly {fuzzyMatch, createFuzzySearch, 
     normalizeText}
       - type re-exports.
     6. Write docs/naming.md (no code change).

     Verification

     - pnpm test → still 77 pass / 7 expected-fail, same 7 test IDs failing as
     before
     (capture the baseline list first). Any change in pass/fail counts =
     regression.
     - pnpm lint:types → exit 0.
     - pnpm build → succeeds; dist/index.d.ts public exports identical to a
     pre-refactor baseline (the critical gate — the package exports key off this
     file).
     - Grep guard: no module imports "upward" (grep -rn "from \"./search\"" 
     src/match.ts
     etc. → empty); grep -rn "1\.5\|0\.9\|1\.6" src/fuzzy.ts src/match.ts → only
     via

     stay
     internal to shared.ts here; that request would later re-export them).
     - Bug fixes 1–6 (this refactor precedes them).

  scoring vocabulary," but they fail the shared test. Localizing them with their

  tier ladder). Grouping into a SCORES namespace reads clean at call sites too
  (SCORES.PREFIX, SCORES.CHUNK_LONG).

  Four nits, all cosmetic:

  1. Dead export in match.ts (line 12). export const SCORES — nothing imports it
  (grep confirms no importers). fuzzy.ts's is local const. Make both local
  const for consistency, or export both intentionally — but right now it's
  asymmetric with no consumer.
  2. as const missing. const SCORES = { … } — properties widen to number and the
  object is mutable. const SCORES = { … } as const makes them readonly literal
  types, blocks accidental mutation, zero runtime cost.
  3. Missing semicolons after both } object literals (fuzzy.ts:19, match.ts:21)
  — rest of the files terminate statements with ;. A formatter pass fixes it.
  4. Leftover import shape fuzzy.ts:8-10 — { isValidWordBoundary, } spread over
  three lines after the other imports were removed; collapses to one line.

  One doc drift to note: docs/naming.md still says score constants live in
  shared.ts as flat SCORE_*/CHUNK_*. Now stale — they're SCORES.* in
  fuzzy.ts/match.ts. Worth fixing when the refactor gets committed.

  Two same-named SCORES objects in sibling modules isn't a collision
  (module-scoped), just noting it's grep-ambiguous — fine to keep.

  oxfmt's own default output — is double quotes + semicolons. The config sets
  neither option, so the defaults win. The claim is backwards, and the config
  files don't even satisfy their own formatter.

  Two cleanup options:
  1. Fix the misleading comment and run pnpm format on the two configs, then
  --amend the tooling commit so it's self-consistent.

● Tree-shaking — yes, it works now, with one gap. Everything tree-shaking needs
  is in place:
  - ESM output — type: "module", exports.import → dist/index.mjs, emitCJS: 
  false. Tree-shaking requires ESM; satisfied.
  - Side-effect-free modules — every file is pure top-level const/function
  declarations. No top-level calls, no global mutation, no console, no IIFE. new
  Set(…) in shared.ts is a pure initializer. So a bundler can safely drop
  unused exports.
  - Granular named exports — fuzzyMatch, createFuzzySearch, normalizeText are
  independent. Importing only normalizeText drops match/fuzzy/search entirely;
  importing only fuzzyMatch drops the createFuzzySearch/sortByScore path.

  The gap: package.json has no "sideEffects": false. Vite/Rollup/esbuild
  tree-shake pure ESM anyway via static analysis, but webpack (and conservative
  setups) won't drop unused modules without that flag. It's a one-line,
  universal win. Caveat: the lib is ~13 kB and fuzzyMatch pulls in most of it
  transitively, so real savings are modest — the clean win is a
  normalizeText-only consumer.

  The module split doesn't change any of this — unbuild bundles to a single
  index.mjs regardless; downstream shaking keys off that bundle's export purity,
  which is good.

  Two decisions:

● User answered Claude's questions:
  ⎿  · src/test.ts is stray database code (createConnection/Connection, 
     undefined names), untracked, imported by nothing. It's the only thing 
     failing `tsc --noEmit`. Delete it? → Delete it (Recommended)
     · Add "sideEffects": false to package.json for reliable tree-shaking across
     all bundlers (incl. webpack)? → Add it (Recommended)

● fzf confirms the direction on bug 1: any non-alphanumeric before an
  alphanumeric is a boundary, with /,:;| as explicit delimiters. Fuse's docs

● Research done — four libraries, mapped to the exact choices in these fixes.
  Here's how the field handles each, and where my in-progress fixes land.

  The two families

  Tiered / substring — match-sorter (Kent C. Dodds) is mikrofuzz's twin:
  discrete rankings CASE_SENSITIVE_EQUAL > EQUAL > STARTS_WITH > 
  WORD_STARTS_WITH > CONTAINS > ACRONYM > MATCHES > NO_MATCH, tie-broken by
  locale compare. That's almost exactly mikrofuzz's ladder (0 / 0.1 / 0.5 /
  0.9-1 / 2 / 2+) — the one tier mikrofuzz lacks is ACRONYM ("us" → "United
  States").

  Continuous / bonus-scored — fzf (Smith-Waterman + bonuses) and uFuzzy score a
  match by summing bonuses for boundary starts, consecutive runs, camelCase, and
  density. Fuse.js is the outlier: Bitap edit-distance, score = 
  errors/patternLen + proximity/distance, threshold 0.6 — it buys typo 
  tolerance, which neither mikrofuzz nor match-sorter attempt.

  Per-fix verdict

  Fix: Bug 1 — punctuation is a boundary; tokenize on non-alnum
  Industry practice: uFuzzy's default interSplit = [^A-Za-z\d']+; fzf treats any

  non-alphanumeric before alphanumeric as a boundary, with /,:;| as explicit
  delimiters
  Alignment: ✅ Strong. My /[^\p{L}\p{N}_]+/u matches uFuzzy's idea and is more
  correct (Unicode-aware). I keep _ (snake_case); uFuzzy keeps '. match-sorter
  is space-only here — i.e. it has mikrofuzz's old bug.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Fix: Bug 2/3 — walk to the boundary occurrence, highlight the real word
  Industry practice: fzf finds the best alignment, not the first; uFuzzy returns

  exact info.ranges
  Alignment: ✅ Standard. "First indexOf" is nobody's design.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Fix: Bug 5 — empty query → null
  Industry practice: uFuzzy: empty needle → filter returns null, not match-all
  Alignment: ✅ Matches uFuzzy, and consistent with mikrofuzz's own
  createFuzzySearch → []. (Some filter-UIs return all for empty — a product
  choice, but it'd contradict the existing behavior.)
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Fix: Bug 6 — highlight width from normalized length
  Industry practice: Everyone returns accurate ranges
  Alignment: ✅ Pure correctness.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Fix: Bug 4 — flat multi-word score (drop the +0.2·n penalty)
  Industry practice: No library penalizes matching more terms. uFuzzy: "matching

  additional search terms improves ranking." fzf: more matched  chars never
  systematically worse
  Alignment: ⚠️ Partial — see below

  The one place to decide: bug 4

  My current fix makes the multi-word tier a flat 1.5 — that removes the
  penalty, which is the bug. But industry doesn't stop at "not worse"; uFuzzy
  and fzf make a more complete / more specific match rank better. That's also
  exactly what KNOWN-ISSUES feature request #5 (match-density) is reaching for,
  and it's the same signal that would tame the long-text hazard (uFuzzy sorts by
  matched-chars ÷ span; fzf penalizes gaps).

  Sources: match-sorter · uFuzzy · fzf algo.go + DeepWiki · Fuse.js

  match.ts is written; search.ts and the tests aren't yet — so the multi-word
  model is still open. How do you want it?

● User answered Claude's questions:
  ⎿  · Multi-word tier scoring — how should matching more query words rank? → 
     What about having this as a separately exported function or option?
     · Add an ACRONYM tier (the one rung match-sorter has that mikrofuzz lacks)?
     → Also an option?

● Good instinct, but let me split it — one of these should be an option, the
  other shouldn't.

  Multi-word (bug 4): don't make it an option. The current behavior isn't a
  preference knob, it's a defect — "more words ranks worse" is nonsense no
  caller would opt into. So there's no "flat vs penalize" toggle worth shipping;
  you just pick the correct behavior and bake it in. Flat 1.5 is the minimal
  correct fix.

  The real thing you're reaching for — let callers control ranking — is better
  served the way uFuzzy does it: don't add a scoring flag per decision, expose 
  the raw signals and let callers Array.sort themselves. uFuzzy's explicit
  design is "a simple Array.sort() with access to each match's stats/counters
  rather than a black-box composite score." That maps exactly to your own
  KNOWN-ISSUES feature requests: #2 expose per-field scores, #4 export tier 
  constants, #5 a density signal. Give those and a caller can implement "reward
  specificity" (or any ranking) without mikrofuzz hardcoding a policy. One or
  two exports beats a pile of scoring booleans.

  Acronym: yes, an option makes sense — but as opt-in (acronym?: boolean,
  default off, since "us"→"United States" adds noise many don't want), and it's
  a genuinely new feature, not a bug fix. match-sorter bakes it in as a
  permanent tier; making it opt-in is the friendlier choice.

  Where that leaves scope: making 7 pass is bug fixing (no API change needed).
  Options + new exports + an acronym tier are a feature pass — and they're best
  designed together, once, so the options object and exports are coherent rather
  than accreted one flag at a time. That's also where feature requests #1–#5
  live.

  On "separately exported function": worth noting the internal matchField isn't
  a clean public export — it takes preprocessed args (normalizedField,
  fieldWords). The clean public levers are the tier constants (#4) and per-field
  scores (#2), not the raw scorer.

  So — how do you want to sequence it?

     mikrofuzz v0.2.0 — configurable scoring + finish the bug fixes

     Context

     Two things land together in one release. (1) The six known bugs are being
     fixed to
     "make 7 pass" — match.ts already has the fixes (punctuation boundaries,
     occurrence-
     walking, flat multi-word, normalized-length highlight width), but search.ts
     and
     known-issues.test.ts aren't done, so the tree is currently RED. (2) The
     user chose
     to design a configurable-scoring feature API first, covering KNOWN-ISSUES
     feature
     requests #1–#5 plus an opt-in acronym tier. Both ship as v0.2.0.

     Design decisions (this session): field ranking control is penalty
     (additive,
     demote-only, ≥0); ACRONYM tier = 1.8 (above CONTAINS); ship matchDensity.
     Grounded in research: match-sorter (tier ladder twin), uFuzzy (expose
     signals + let
     callers sort; punctuation splitting), fzf (any non-alnum before alnum =
     boundary),
     Fuse.js (per-key weights, contrast — it's Bitap/edit-distance).

     Everything is additive → non-breaking at runtime; the public .d.ts grows
     (intended).

     Public API (final)

     // src/types.ts
     export type FuzzyResult<T> = {
        item: T;
        score: number;                 // min EFFECTIVE (post-penalty) score acr
     texts
        matches: FuzzyMatches;         // per-text highlight lists (unchanged)
        scores: Array<number | null>;  // NEW: per-text effective scores, parall
     to matches
     };

     export type FuzzySearchField<T = unknown> = {
        getText: (item: T) => string | null | Array<string | null>;
        strategy?: FuzzySearchStrategy; // default "smart"
        acronym?: boolean;              // default false
        penalty?: number;               // added to this field's score; default 
     keep >= 0
     };

     export type FuzzySearchOptions<T = unknown> = {
        key?: string;
        getText?: (item: T) => Array<string | null>; // now generic — drops the 
     `unknown` cast
        strategy?: FuzzySearchStrategy;
        acronym?: boolean;                            // legacy key/getText path
        fields?: Array<FuzzySearchField<T>>;          // supersedes 
     key/getText/strategy/acronym
     };

     // src/scores.ts (NEW value module — single source of truth)
     export const SCORES = {
        EXACT: 0, NORMALIZED_EXACT: 0.1, PREFIX: 0.5, BOUNDARY_EXACT: 0.9,
        BOUNDARY: 1, MULTI_WORD: 1.5, ACRONYM: 1.8, CONTAINS: 2,
     } as const;
     // "any score > CONTAINS is a fuzzy match" — the fuzzy floor stays 
     internal.

     - createFuzzySearch<T>(collection: T[], options?: FuzzySearchOptions<T>).
     - matchDensity(ranges: HighlightRanges): number — matched-chars ÷ span over
     ONE
     text's ranges: matched = Σ(end-start+1), span = lastEnd-firstStart+1,
     span > 0 ? matched/span : 0.
     - New barrel exports: export { SCORES } from "./scores", export { 
     matchDensity } from "./density".

     Semantics

     - penalty (demote-only): applied in search.ts, NOT matchField. Field
     effective = rawTierScore + (penalty ?? 0). Item score = min(effective 
     across texts);
     scores[i] = that effective value (so score === min of non-null scores
     holds).
     Idiom for "body never outranks title": penalty: SCORES.CONTAINS.
     - fields precedence: if options.fields present, ignore
     key/getText/strategy/
     acronym. Normalize BOTH paths into one flat spec list {text, strategy, 
     acronym, penalty}
     at preprocess time → one indexing rule. A field getText returning an array
     expands
     in place (one matches/scores slot per text); single string → clean 1:1.
     - acronym tier (opt-in, SCORES.ACRONYM = 1.8): fires only when enabled AND
     all
     earlier tiers missed, right before the fuzzy fallback, query length ≥ 2.
     Derive
     initials from normalizedField word-starts via isValidWordBoundary (no
     ordered-word
     plumbing; gives offsets for ranges). initials.indexOf(normalizedQuery)
     (contiguous
     run, match-sorter style); ranges highlight each initial [o, o]. matchField
     gains a
     single acronym: boolean param.

     File changes

     - src/scores.ts (new): the SCORES as const object.
     - src/density.ts (new): matchDensity.
     - src/match.ts: drop local SCORES, import { SCORES } from "./scores"; add
     acronym param + acronymMatch helper (after CONTAINS, before fuzzy
     dispatch); keep
     the already-applied bug fixes (boundaryOccurrence, flat MULTI_WORD,
     normalizedQueryLen
     widths).
     - src/fuzzy.ts: rename internal SCORES → CHUNK_SCORES (comment that BASE:2
     equals SCORES.CONTAINS by design — do NOT share the binding).
     - src/search.ts (biggest): wire splitWords in place of all four .split(" ")
     (completes bug #1 — splitWords currently has zero call-sites); add
     empty-query guard
     to fuzzyMatch (bug #5) returning null; fuzzyMatch returns scores: 
     [result[0]];
     normalize options → flat spec list; per spec compute effective = raw + 
     penalty,
     accumulate scores/matches, bestScore = min(effective); emit {item, score, 
     matches, scores}.
     Both legacy and fields paths share ONE tokenization/preprocess helper (else
     bug #1
     reappears for per-field).

       70  
       71  ## Scoring
       72  
       73 -Lower scores indicate better matches:                         
       73 +Lower scores indicate better matches. Import `SCORES` to filte
          +r or re-rank by                                               
       74 +tier instead of hardcoding numbers:                           
       75  
       75 -| Score | Match Type |                                        
       76 -|-------|------------|                                        
       77 -| 0 | Exact match |                                           
       78 -| 0.1 | Case/diacritics-insensitive exact match |             
       79 -| 0.5 | Starts with query |                                   
       80 -| 0.9 | Contains at word boundary (exact case) |              
       81 -| 1 | Contains at word boundary |                             
       82 -| 1.5+ | Contains all query words (any order) |               
       83 -| 2 | Contains query anywhere |                               
       84 -| 2+ | Fuzzy match (fewer chunks = better) |                  
       76 +| Score | Constant | Match Type |                             
       77 +|-------|----------|------------|                             
       78 +| 0 | `SCORES.EXACT` | Exact match |                          
       79 +| 0.1 | `SCORES.NORMALIZED_EXACT` | Case/diacritics-insensitiv
          +e exact match |                                               
       80 +| 0.5 | `SCORES.PREFIX` | Starts with query |                 
       81 +| 0.9 | `SCORES.BOUNDARY_EXACT` | Contains at word boundary (e
          +xact case) |                                                  
       82 +| 1 | `SCORES.BOUNDARY` | Contains at word boundary |         
       83 +| 1.5 | `SCORES.MULTI_WORD` | Contains all query words (any or
          +der) |                                                        
       84 +| 1.8 | `SCORES.ACRONYM` | Matches word initials (opt-in, see 
          +`acronym`) |                                                  
       85 +| 2 | `SCORES.CONTAINS` | Contains query anywhere |           
       86 +| 2+ | — | Fuzzy match (fewer chunks = better) |              
       87  
       88 +Any score greater than `SCORES.CONTAINS` is a fuzzy-fallback m
          +atch:                                                         
       89 +                                                              
       90 +```typescript                                                 
       91 +import { SCORES } from "@mmmike/mikrofuzz";                   
       92 +const solid = results.filter((r) => r.score <= SCORES.CONTAINS
          +); // drop fuzzy chains                                       
       93 +```                                                           
       94 +                                                              
       95 +> **Long text:** fuzzy strategies assemble short queries out o
          +f scattered chunks,                                           
       96 +> so over document-length text almost anything "matches". Scop
          +e `smart`/`aggressive`                                        
       97 +> to short labels (titles, names); use `strategy: "off"` for l
          +ong body text.                                                
       98 +                                                              
       99  ## Search Strategies
      100  
      101  ```typescript
     ...
      108  | `"aggressive"` | Classic fuzzy matching (any letters in orde
           r) |
      109  | `"off"` | Only exact, prefix, and contains matching |
      110  
      111 +## Per-Field Configuration                                    
      112 +                                                              
      113 +Give each field its own strategy, opt into acronym matching, a
          +nd add a `penalty`                                            
      114 +that demotes a field. A field's effective score is `tierScore 
          ++ penalty`; the                                               
      115 +item's `score` is the best (lowest) across fields, and every f
          +ield's effective                                              
      116 +score is returned in `result.scores` (parallel to `matches`). 
      117 +                                                              
      118 +```typescript                                                 
      119 +const search = createFuzzySearch(posts, {                     
      120 +  fields: [                                                   
      121 +    { getText: (p) => p.title, strategy: "smart" },           
      122 +    // contains-only, and never let body outrank a title match
          +:                                                             
      123 +    { getText: (p) => p.body, strategy: "off", penalty: SCORES
          +.CONTAINS },                                                  
      124 +  ],                                                          
      125 +});                                                           
      126 +```                                                           
      127 +                                                              
      128 +`fields` supersedes `key`/`getText`/`strategy`/`acronym`. A fi
          +eld's `getText` may                                           
      129 +return a single string (1:1 with `matches`/`scores`) or an arr
          +ay (expanded in place).                                       
      130 +                                                              
      131  ## API Reference
      132  
      133  ### `createFuzzySearch<T>(collection, options?)`
     ...
      135  Creates a reusable search function for a collection.
      136  
      137  **Options:**
      105 -- `key?: string` - Property name to search (for object arrays)
      106 -- `getText?: (item: T) => Array<string | null>` - Custom text 
          -extraction                                                    
      107 -- `strategy?: "smart" | "aggressive" | "off"` - Matching strat
          -egy                                                           
      138 +- `key?: string` — Property name to search (for object arrays)
      139 +- `getText?: (item: T) => Array<string | null>` — Custom text 
          +extraction (typed to `T`)                                     
      140 +- `strategy?: "smart" | "aggressive" | "off"` — Matching strat
          +egy                                                           
      141 +- `acronym?: boolean` — Enable the word-initials tier (default
          + `false`)                                                     
      142 +- `fields?: FuzzySearchField<T>[]` — Per-field config (superse
          +des the above)                                                
      143  
      144  **Returns:** `(query: string) => FuzzyResult<T>[]`
      145  
      146  ### `fuzzyMatch(text, query)`
      147  
      113 -One-off fuzzy match for a single string.                      
      148 +One-off fuzzy match for a single string. **Returns:** `FuzzyRe
          +sult<string> | null`.                                         
      149  
      115 -**Returns:** `FuzzyResult<string> | null`                     
      116 -                                                              
      150  ### `normalizeText(str)`
      151  
      152  Normalize text (lowercase, remove diacritics).
      153  
      154 +### `matchDensity(ranges)`                                    
      155 +                                                              
      156 +Matched characters ÷ inclusive span for one field's `Highlight
          +Ranges` (1 = a single                                         
      157 +solid run; lower = more scattered). A cheap discriminator for 
          +junk fuzzy chains.                                            
      158 +                                                              
      159 +### `SCORES`                                                  
      160 +                                                              
      161 +Frozen object of the tier scores in the Scoring table above.  
      162 +                                                              
      163  ## Types
      164  
      165  ```typescript
     ...
      169  
      170  interface FuzzyResult<T> {
      171    item: T;
      130 -  score: number;                                              
      131 -  matches: FuzzyMatches;                                      
      172 +  score: number;                // min effective score across 
          +fields                                                        
      173 +  matches: FuzzyMatches;        // per-text highlight ranges  
      174 +  scores: Array<number | null>; // per-text effective scores, 
          +parallel to matches

      176  
      134 -interface FuzzySearchOptions {                                
      177 +interface FuzzySearchField<T = unknown> {                     
      178 +  getText: (item: T) => string | null | Array<string | null>; 
      179 +  strategy?: "off" | "smart" | "aggressive";                  
      180 +  acronym?: boolean;                                          
      181 +  penalty?: number; // added to the field's score; higher demo
          +tes it

      185    key?: string;
      136 -  getText?: (item: unknown) => Array<string | null>;          
      186 +  getText?: (item: T) => Array<string | null>;

● Update(docs/naming.md)
  ⎿  Added 22 lines
      119  - **`start` / `end`** — the bounds of a range or chunk.
      120  - **`SMART_MIN_CHUNK`** — the smart strategy's minimum mid-wor
           d lookahead width (the `3` in
      121    `Math.min(3, …)`).
      122 +                                                              
      123 +## v0.2.0 additions                                           
      124 +                                                              
      125 +- **`field-config`** (`FuzzySearchField`) — per-field `getText
          +`/`strategy`/`acronym`/`penalty`.                             
      126 +- **`penalty`** — number added to a field's score; higher demo
          +tes it (lower is better).                                     
      127 +  Demote-only by design (kept ≥ 0).                           
      128 +- **`acronym`** — opt-in tier matching word-initials; `acronym
          +Match` reads initials via the                                 
      129 +  `wordRun` regex `/[\p{L}\p{N}_]+/u` (same word definition as
          + `splitWords`).                                               
      130 +- **`scores`** — per-text effective (post-penalty) scores on `
          +FuzzyResult`, parallel to `matches`.                          
      131 +- **`SCORES`** (`src/scores.ts`) — exported tier constants; si
          +ngle source of truth, imported by                             
      132 +  `match.ts`, re-exported by the barrel.                      
      133 +- **`CHUNK_SCORES`** (`src/fuzzy.ts`) — internal fuzzy-chunk b
          +onuses (renamed from `SCORES` to

          +gn, not by a shared binding.

          +usive span helper.

❯ Worh doing any perf tests and comparing to other libs?                        

● Short answer: a light internal benchmark is worth it; a cross-lib shootout 
  only as fair positioning, not a speed brag. Here's the reasoning.

  Where perf actually matters for mikrofuzz. Preprocessing (normalize +
  splitWords + Set per field) is one-time at createFuzzySearch. Query-time is
  the hot path. mikrofuzz's niche is short curated fields, client-side (its own
  hazard note says scope fuzzy to short labels) — so it's not competing with
  big-corpus engines, and absolute speed matters less than correctness/ranking
  here.

  What a benchmark would actually catch — and why now. v0.2.0 added things worth
  a baseline: boundaryOccurrence now loops indexOf (was single), multi-word
  ranges do a boundary lookup per word, acronym runs matchAll per field, and
  there's a Set per field. None look pathological, but there's no baseline to
  prove v0.2.0 didn't regress v0.1 or blow up on a bad input. That's the real
  value: regression guard + a documented ceiling (items/ms), not chasing a
  number.

  Cross-lib is apples-to-oranges unless framed carefully.
  - Fuse.js is Bitap/edit-distance — it does typo tolerance mikrofuzz doesn't.
  Comparing raw ns/op is unfair; it's doing more work for a different
  capability.
  - uFuzzy / fuzzysort are speed-optimized (typed arrays, single-pass). On large
  lists they'll win — that's expected and fine to document, not a failing.
  - match-sorter is the fair peer (same tier-ladder model, no typos). That's the
  honest comparison.

  So a comparison is worth it for positioning ("great for lists up to ~N; reach
  for uFuzzy/fuzzysort on 100k+"), on the same non-typo task, with feature
  differences stated. Numbers as context, not bragging rights.

  Tooling fit. Vitest ships bench (tinybench) — zero new runtime deps, drops
  into the existing setup. Cross-lib needs the competitors as devDeps. And a
  third cheap dimension: bundle size (min+gzip) — relevant for a zero-dep client
  lib; dist grew when v0.2.0 landed.

  Note the v0.2.0 code is still uncommitted on main awaiting your branch/commit
  call — benchmarks are separate work and would add their own files/devDeps.

● Done — benchmarks and bundle sizes measured. Here's the picture.

  Query speed (per query, over a list of short 3-word titles)

  ┌──────────────┬───────────┬───────────┬───────────────┐
  │     Lib      │ 2k items  │ 10k items │ vs mikrofuzz  │
  ├──────────────┼───────────┼───────────┼───────────────┤
  │ uFuzzy       │ ~0.042 ms │ ~0.265 ms │ ~7× faster    │
  ├──────────────┼───────────┼───────────┼───────────────┤
  │ mikrofuzz    │ ~0.30 ms  │ ~1.75 ms  │ —             │
  ├──────────────┼───────────┼───────────┼───────────────┤
  │ match-sorter │ ~0.42 ms  │ ~2.33 ms  │ ~1.35× slower │
  ├──────────────┼───────────┼───────────┼───────────────┤
  │ Fuse.js      │ ~2.3 ms   │ ~12.3 ms  │ ~7× slower    │
  └──────────────┴───────────┴───────────┴───────────────┘

  mikrofuzz is mid-pack: comfortably faster than match-sorter (its fair peer)
  and Fuse, but uFuzzy is ~7× faster and is the reference for speed. Scaling is
  linear (5× the items → ~6× the time) — so v0.2.0's per-field Sets,
  occurrence-walking, and acronym matchAll added no pathological blowup. That's
  the main regression-guard result.

  Index build (one-time)

  mikrofuzz createFuzzySearch preprocesses ~8.4 ms / 10k items; Fuse builds ~17×
  faster (0.48 ms). Both are one-time setup — negligible for as-you-type UI,
  where query cost dominates.

  Bundle size (gzip of the published entry, all unminified, same method)

  ┌──────────────┬────────┬─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │     Lib      │  gzip  │                  runtime deps                   │
  ├──────────────┼────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ mikrofuzz    │ 2.52   │ none                                            │
  │              │ kB     │                                                 │
  ├──────────────┼────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ match-sorter │ 4.08   │ +@babel/runtime, remove-accents (not counted →  │
  │              │ kB     │ real footprint larger)                          │
  ├──────────────┼────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ uFuzzy       │ 8.65   │ none                                            │
  │              │ kB     │                                                 │
  ├──────────────┼────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Fuse.js      │ 12.79  │ none                                            │
  │              │ kB     │                                                 │
  └──────────────┴────────┴─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

  mikrofuzz is the smallest, by a wide margin, with zero deps. (A consumer's
  bundler minifies further; I couldn't minify locally — no esbuild binary /
  network — but the relative comparison holds since every lib was measured the
  same way.)

  Fairness caveats (important)

  - Fuse's 7× gap buys typo tolerance (Bitap edit-distance) that mikrofuzz
  doesn't attempt — not an apples-to-apples speed loss.
  - uFuzzy is typed-array optimized for exactly this; being ~7× faster is
  expected, not a mikrofuzz failing.
  - Single dataset shape (short titles); real numbers vary with field length and
  query type.

  Verdict

  mikrofuzz's sweet spot is small-to-medium client-side lists (≤~10k short 
  fields) where tiny size + zero deps + tier-based ranking matter more than raw
  throughput. Sub-2 ms/query through 10k is fine for as-you-type. For 100k+
  corpora reach for uFuzzy/fuzzysort; for misspelling tolerance, Fuse.

  @leeoniya/ufuzzy), bench/compare.bench.ts, and a bench script — on top of the
  still-uncommitted v0.2.0 work, all on main. Two calls for you: (1) want a
  short Performance section in the README with this positioning + the 2.5 kB

❯ What lessons can we learn from ufuzzy?                                        

● Good question — uFuzzy being ~7× faster is worth dissecting. Let me confirm
  its actual mechanism (not just infer) before drawing lessons.

● Fetch(https://raw.githubusercontent.com/leeoniya/uFuzzy/main/README.md)
  ⎿  Received 36.4KB (200 OK)

● Confirmed uFuzzy's architecture, so these lessons are grounded, not guessed.
  Two of them mikrofuzz already adopted this session (splitWords = uFuzzy's
  interSplit tokenization; scores/matchDensity = its expose-signals philosophy),
  which validates the direction. Here's the rest.

  The core insight

  uFuzzy does two things mikrofuzz doesn't:
  1. It matches with the native RegExp engine, not hand-rolled per-character JS
  loops. It compiles the needle into a RegExp (lazy quantifiers + char classes)
  and lets the C regex engine scan. mikrofuzz's
  smartFuzzyMatch/aggressiveFuzzyMatch are interpreted char-by-char loops —
  that's most of the 7× gap.
  2. Cheap filter before expensive work. Its filter() phase does a fast regex
  reduce to candidate indices; only survivors go to info(), which re-compiles
  heavier regexes to extract ranges/stats. mikrofuzz computes full matches +
  ranges for every item, every query.

  Your cheap tiers (exact/prefix/contains) are already native
  (indexOf/startsWith), near uFuzzy speed. The gap is almost entirely the fuzzy 
  fallback running full work on every non-matching item.

  Perf lessons (ranked by value/risk)

  L1 — Regex pre-gate the fuzzy tier (highest value, low risk). Before running
  the hand-rolled chunk scorer on an item, test() it against a
  one-time-per-query lazy-subsequence regex (/t[^k]*k[^n]*n.../). Native
  rejection of the ~majority that can't match, then run the exact scorer only on
  survivors. Preserves current scoring exactly — it only gates. This is
  uFuzzy's filter/info split applied surgically to the one slow path.

  L2 — Hoist per-query work out of the per-item loop. The fuzzy matchers
  re-derive query state per item. Compile the gate regex + query tokens once per
  query, reuse across all items.

  L3 — Fully regex-ify the aggressive tier. It's a plain subsequence → a regex
  with capture groups gives you chunk positions directly; score from the
  captures. Easy win. Caveat: the smart tier's rule ("chunk starts at a word
  boundary or runs 3+ chars") is regex-awkward — keep it hand-rolled, but gated
  by L1.

  L4 — Trim per-match allocation. Tuples/arrays/objects per item per tier create
  GC pressure in the hot loop. Minor next to L1.

  Realistic outcome: L1–L3 could close much of the gap on fuzzy-heavy queries
  (the slow path). Prefix/contains queries are already fast, so the win is
  uneven. mikrofuzz stays "great for its niche," not a uFuzzy-killer — the rest
  of the gap is architectural.

  Design lessons (non-perf)

  L5 — Expose match-stat components, not just a composite score. uFuzzy
  deliberately avoids a "black-box score" — it hands you counters (start offset,
  density, term count, ranges) and you Array.sort. You've started this (scores,
  matchDensity); going further (surface the per-tier signals) fits the same
  philosophy.

  L6 — Boundary strictness as its own axis. uFuzzy's interLft/interRgt model
  "match anywhere / loose boundary / strict boundary" as one orthogonal knob.
  mikrofuzz conflates this into strategy (off/smart/aggressive). Separating "how
  fuzzy" from "how boundary-strict" would be cleaner.

  L7 — Scope honesty. uFuzzy is blunt: fast flat-list filter, not a
  typo-tolerant ranker. Own your niche in the docs the same way (small lists,
  tier ranking, 2.5 kB, zero deps).

  What NOT to copy

  Don't rewrite into a regex-only, index-free, typed-array engine — that is
  uFuzzy. You'd lose the readable tier ladder, the ranking quality, and the tiny
  size, and still not beat the original. The 7× is the price of a different
  design point; closing it fully means abandoning yours.

  The single highest-leverage, lowest-risk move is L1 — a native regex gate on
  the fuzzy tier, behavior-identical, targeting exactly the slow path the
  benchmark exposed. Want me to prototype it and re-run the bench to measure the
  actual gain? (Still no commits made — v0.2.0 + the bench deps remain
  uncommitted on main pending your call.)

✻ Crunched for 2m 7s

❯ Yeah let's give it a bash!                                                    

● Let's build it. L1 = a native regex "subsequence gate" — if a field doesn't
  even contain the query characters in order, no fuzzy strategy can match it
  (both matchers require subsequence), so we skip the hand-rolled loop.
  Behavior-identical, only gates. I'll also bundle the query-derived args into
  one object (built once per query) so matchField doesn't grow to 9 params.

● Behavior-identical — 96 tests still green, typecheck + oxlint clean. Now the
  payoff: re-running the bench to measure the gate's effect.

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

● Worked — and the gain is real. The subsequence gate (L1) plus hoisting query
  state into one object (L2) roughly doubled query throughput,
  behavior-identical (96 tests still green).

  Before → after (query time)

  ┌──────────┬──────────────────┬──────────────────┬─────────┬─────────────┐
  │ Dataset  │      before      │      after       │ speedup │   gap vs    │
  │          │                  │                  │         │   uFuzzy    │
  ├──────────┼──────────────────┼──────────────────┼─────────┼─────────────┤
  │ 2k items │ 559 hz (~0.30    │ 909 hz (~0.18    │ 1.6×    │ 7.0× → 4.1× │
  │          │ ms/q)            │ ms/q)            │         │             │
  ├──────────┼──────────────────┼──────────────────┼─────────┼─────────────┤
  │ 10k      │ 95 hz (~1.75     │ 183 hz (~0.91    │ 1.9×    │ 6.6× → 4.0× │
  │ items    │ ms/q)            │ ms/q)            │         │             │
  └──────────┴──────────────────┴──────────────────┴─────────┴─────────────┘

  Bigger win at 10k — more non-matching items to reject cheaply. mikrofuzz now
  beats match-sorter by ~2.3–2.5× (was ~1.3×), and stays ~50× ahead of Fuse.

  Why it worked

  The benchmark's slow queries (tknmatchr, modidx) are sparse — most items reach
  the fuzzy fallback and fail late in the hand-rolled loop. The gate is a
  one-per-query regex (t[^]*k[^]*n[^]*…); a field that fails it can't match any
  fuzzy strategy (both require the query as a subsequence), so we test()-reject
  in native code before the JS loop ever runs. Pure necessary-condition filter →
  identical results, confirmed by the unchanged 96-test suite.

  The change

  ~15 lines: buildFuzzyGate in fuzzy.ts, one test() before the fuzzy dispatch in
  match.ts, and query-derived state
  (query/normalizedQuery/queryWords/fuzzyGate) bundled into a MatchQuery built
  once per query (which also fixed the 8→was-going-to-be-9 param creep —
  matchField now takes 6).

  Honest ceiling

  Still ~4× behind uFuzzy — that's architectural (it matches entirely via native
  regex; mikrofuzz's smart tier's "boundary-start or 3+ run" rule is
  regex-awkward and stays hand-rolled). L1 was the cheap, high-value 2× win;
  remaining gains (L3, regex-ifying the aggressive tier) are smaller and harder.
  I'd stop here — good return, design intact.

  This adds to the uncommitted pile (still on main): v0.2.0 + bench deps + now
  the perf gate. Want me to keep going on L3, or shall we sort out committing
  all this? I still need your go-ahead before any commit — and a call on whether
  the bench devDeps stay.

❯ /**                                                                           
   * Fuzzy search library                                                       
   * Adapted from @nozbe/microfuzz with Vite SSR compatibility                  
   *                                                                            
   * Scoring (lower = better):                                                  
   * - 0:    Exact match                                                        
   * - 0.1:  Case/diacritics-insensitive exact match                            
   * - 0.5:  Starts with query                                                  
   * - 0.9:  Contains query at word boundary (exact case)                       
   * - 1:    Contains query at word boundary                                    
   * - 1.5:  Contains all query words (in any order)                            
   * - 1.8:  Matches word initials (acronym tier, opt-in)                       
   * - 2:    Contains query anywhere                                            
   * - 2+:   Fuzzy match (fewer chunks = better)                                
                                                                                
  Are numbers the best way to represent this?                                   

● Short answer: numbers are right for one of the two jobs they're currently
  doing, and wrong for the other.

  Numbers are good as the sort key

  - Sorting is a trivial a.score - b.score.
  - penalty composes by addition — "demote this field" is just +n. A categorical
  tier can't be added to.
  - The fuzzy tail is genuinely continuous (base 2 + chunk bonuses), so it needs
  a real number, not a label.

  Keep the number for ordering. That part's fine.

  Numbers are weak as the tier identity

  The same float is also being asked to answer "what kind of match was this?",
  and there it's lossy and fragile:

  1. Penalties and the fuzzy tail blur the tiers. A prefix match (0.5) with
  penalty: 2 becomes 2.5 — now it "looks like" a fuzzy score. Once penalties or
  fuzzy are in play, you can't reliably reverse-map a number to a tier. So
  SCORES constants help you set thresholds but don't let a result tell you how
  it matched.
  2. The float gaps pretend to be a metric they aren't. Is
  EXACT→NORMALIZED_EXACT (0.1) "closer" than PREFIX→BOUNDARY_EXACT (0.4)? No —
  the gaps are arbitrary ordinal anchors chosen to leave room, not distances.
  Floats invite reading meaning into spacing that isn't there.
  3. Narrow room makes new tiers fragile. ACRONYM had to be squeezed into
  1.5–2.0; the fuzzy floor sits right at 2.2. Adding a tier means hunting for a
  gap.
  4. The header comment you pasted is a hand-maintained duplicate of SCORES —
  guaranteed to drift. It should point at the constants, not restate them.

  Best representation

  The number is the sort key; add the tier as a category. Return an explicit
  tier ("exact" | "prefix" | … | "acronym" | "fuzzy") alongside the score.
  matchField already knows which tier it returned — it's free to surface. Then:
  - filter reads r.tier !== "fuzzy" instead of the magic r.score <= 
  SCORES.CONTAINS;
  - "group by match type" / "why did this rank here" become answerable;
  - the number keeps doing sorting + penalties.

  That's exactly the established split: match-sorter exposes a rankings enum and
  a separate closeness value; uFuzzy exposes raw counters, no single black-box
  score. mikrofuzz already leaned this way with scores/matchDensity — tier is
  the missing categorical half.

  One timely note

  v0.2.0 is unpublished (still uncommitted), and it already added scores next to
  matches — so you have two parallel per-field arrays. Adding tier makes three,
  which is a smell. Now — before it ships — is the free moment to decide: add a
  third parallel array, or consolidate into one fields: Array<{ ranges, score, 
  tier } | null> (keeping top-level score and the v0.1 matches for back-compat).
  After it's published, that choice gets expensive.

  (Polarity — lower=better "error level" — is a separate, smaller question; it's
  a defensible convention and flipping it is breaking for little gain. Not the
  core issue.)

  I'd keep the number and add tier. Want me to implement it — and if so, third
  parallel array or consolidate into a fields struct?

✻ Cooked for 1m 51s

❯ Damn, are we overloading the api?                                             

● Yeah — honestly, partly. And the tell is how it grew: one addition per turn
  (acronym, then scores, then matchDensity, then I pitched tier), each
  individually justifiable, none from a single coherent "users need this" —
  mostly a wishlist (KNOWN-ISSUES) plus my own research suggestions. That's
  accretion, and my tier proposal last turn is the one that tipped it into
  "wait, are we kitchen-sinking this?" Good instinct to stop and check.

  Here's the honest read. Two different things got bundled:

  Correctness — the 6 bug fixes, the perf gate, generic <T>. Zero real API
  growth, everyone benefits, uncontroversial. This is the clean win.

  Configurability — everything else. This is where a 2.5 kB "does one thing
  well" lib roughly doubled its concept count. uFuzzy — the lib we admired —
  deliberately resists exactly this (expose primitives, make the caller sort,
  don't grow options). We went the other way.

  Per-item verdict:

  Addition: Bug fixes + perf gate
  Verdict: keep
  Why: Not API. Pure win.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Addition: Generic FuzzySearchOptions<T>
  Verdict: keep
  Why: Free, removes a cast.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Addition: fields + penalty
  Verdict: keep
  Why: The one config feature with a real motivating case — the blog integration

  that needed two searchers + manual min-merge. Earns its weight.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Addition: scores
  Verdict: keep
  Why: Cheap, and pairs naturally with fields (per-field visibility). The "let
  callers rank" primitive.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Addition: SCORES
  Verdict: lean keep
  Why: One const, low cost — though its value is partly undercut by the
  tier-identity problem I raised.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Addition: matchDensity
  Verdict: cut
  Why: Speculative. No user asked; it's a 5-line util a caller can write.
  Textbook "because we could."
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Addition: acronym
  Verdict: defer/cut
  Why: A whole new tier — scope creep past "fuzzy search." Opt-in, so low blast
  radius, but the clearest accretion.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Addition: tier (my proposal)
  Verdict: don't add now
  Why: Would compound the overload. Revisit only if scores/SCORES prove
  insufficient in practice.

  The lucky part: nothing is committed yet, so trimming is free. Everything's
  sitting uncommitted on main. So the clean move:

  1. Commit correctness as v0.2.0 — bug fixes + perf gate + generic types.
  Small, sharp, shippable, no debate.
  2. Treat configurability as a separate, deliberate v0.3 — and ship only
  fields/penalty (+ scores). Cut matchDensity, hold acronym and tier.

  That keeps mikrofuzz's whole pitch (tiny, focused) intact while still landing
  the one power-feature that solves a documented pain.

  Want me to split it that way — carve the correctness commit and park the
  configurability trimming for a separate branch? Or if you'd rather keep it
  all, that's your call — I just wouldn't add tier on top.
