※ recap: Building mikrofuzz v0.2.0: bug fixes and features are done, tested (96 passing), and uncommitted on main. Next, decide whether to commit correctness first and trim the extra config API (cut matchDensity, hold acronym/tier), or commit it all.

❯ See, we can actually tackle this one different way.                           
                                                                                
  We can export different functions. We are already doing this, right? Let's    
  think about what tools we actually want from this?                            

● Yes — exactly, and that's the better axis. We already export standalone pieces
  (normalizeText, matchDensity, SCORES, and fuzzyMatch is basically a
  primitive). The mistake was under-investing in those and pouring everything
  into createFuzzySearch's options bag instead. Lean the other way.

  The realization: the real atom is "score one string against a query → { score,
  tier, ranges }". Everything else — collections, multi-field, penalties,
  custom ranking — is composition on top of that atom. And right now that atom
  (matchField) is buried internal, while fuzzyMatch is a thin no-options wrapper
  of it. Expose the atom richly and the fat options dissolve.

  The toolkit (3 layers)

  1. The primitive — fuzzyMatch(text, query, { strategy?, acronym? }) → { score,
  tier, ranges } | null. Stateless, returns the rich result. This is the whole
  engine, exposed. (Returning tier here also answers the numbers-vs-tier
  question — it lives on the atom, not bolted onto an array.)

  2. Collection convenience — createFuzzySearch(list, { key?/getText?, strategy?
  }) → (query) => results[]. Its real reason to exist is the preprocessing 
  cache (normalize + tokenize each item once, reuse across keystrokes) — not the
  options. Keep it thin: strings + key/getText, sorted. Covers ~90% of users.

  3. Building blocks — normalizeText, splitWords (currently internal — export
  it), matchDensity, SCORES, and a Tier union. The vocabulary for people who
  compose.

  Where the fat options go

  ┌─────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │  Was becoming an    │                     New home                      │
  │       option        │                                                   │
  ├─────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ strategy            │ opt on the primitive (+ passthrough on the        │
  │                     │ wrapper)                                          │
  ├─────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ acronym             │ opt on the primitive                              │
  ├─────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ fields              │ caller maps the primitive over fields — ~6 lines, │
  │ (multi-field)       │  full control                                     │
  ├─────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ penalty             │ caller writes score + n (trivial once they have   │
  │                     │ per-field results)                                │
  ├─────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ scores (per-field)  │ falls out — the caller already holds each         │
  │                     │ primitive result                                  │
  ├─────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ tier                │ returned by the primitive                         │
  └─────────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

  The blog-search case ("fuzzy title, contains-only body, body never outranks
  title") becomes a short caller-side loop using fuzzyMatch + SCORES — and it's
  more flexible than any fields/penalty shape we'd have designed, because they
  control the merge.

  Why this is the right call

  It ships less but enables more. The options version could only do the ranking
  shapes we imagined; the primitive lets callers build policies we never thought
  of. That's the uFuzzy lesson (expose primitives, sort it yourself) applied to
  the API, not just the perf. And it kills both worries at once: options bag
  shrinks (overload), tier lives on the atom (representation).

  Two boundaries to pin down

  1. The primitive's shape/name. Enrich fuzzyMatch in place to { score, tier, 
  ranges } (breaking its v0.1 {item, matches, scores} shape — fine pre-1.0), or
  introduce it under a new name (match/score) and leave fuzzyMatch alone?
  2. Where's the convenience line? Does createFuzzySearch stay
  single-field-simple (multi-field = compose), or do we keep one tiny
  multi-field helper so the common case isn't a hand-rolled loop?

  What's your instinct on those two? Once we agree on the primitive shape and
  the convenience line, I'll write it up.

✻ Worked for 1m 42s

❯ Oh we're publishing that as V1.0.0 so let's break the shit out of the api     
                                                                                
  Convenience is genuinely important. But maybe we can think of how we can      
  package it in a nice way? If we think of things like zod/valibot etc, or a    
  fluent interface, or even using a class to create a a searcher that takes in  
  components/strategies?                                                        

● v1.0 with a free hand — good, let's design it right. Quick verdict on the
  three you named, then the synthesis.

  Class + strategies → no. Kills tree-shaking (every method ships whether used
  or not), adds new/this/instances, and it's a lot of machinery for a small
  config space. It clashes with a 2.5 kB functional lib. But the good idea
  buried inside it — injectable strategies — is worth stealing, just
  functionally (below).

  Global fluent builder → mostly no. Great autocomplete, but it's a stateful
  builder with .build() ceremony, poor tree-shaking (one object carrying all
  methods), and per-field config via chaining gets ambiguous
  (.field(...).smart() — which field does .smart() bind to?). Fluent shines for
  a linear single-subject pipeline, not a per-field matrix.

  zod/valibot style → yes, but take the real lesson. valibot's win isn't "add
  builders" — it's compose small, typed, plain-data pieces, and the core 
  consumes plain data. For our config (a list + a few field specs) the plain
  objects basically are that already. Don't build a DSL for a 4-field config.

  The synthesis: data-first core + functional strategy injection

  import { createFuzzySearch, SCORES } from '@mmmike/mikrofuzz';

  // 1. common case — array of strings
  createFuzzySearch(titles)('que');

  // 2. objects, one field — getText as a positional arg, no options bag
  createFuzzySearch(users, u => u.name)('john');

  // 3. multi-field — a plain array of field specs (this replaces the fat 
  `fields`/`penalty` options)
  createFuzzySearch(posts, [
    { text: p => p.title, strategy: 'smart' },
    { text: p => p.body,  strategy: 'off', penalty: SCORES.CONTAINS },
  ])('event loop');

  // 4. functional strategy injection — pass YOUR matcher where a string goes
  createFuzzySearch(items, [
    { text: i => i.code, strategy: myMatcher },   // (normField, normQuery) => 
  [score, ranges] | null
  ]);

  Under it all sits the primitive fuzzyMatch(text, query, { strategy, acronym })
  → { score, tier, ranges }. createFuzzySearch is just the preprocessing-cache
  + map + sort over it.

  Why this is the mikrofuzz-shaped answer:
  - No options bag. Second arg is getText fn or an array of field specs. Config
  is plain data.
  - Functional strategy injection is your "components/strategies" idea done
  right: a strategy is already just a function
  (smartFuzzyMatch/aggressiveFuzzyMatch are functions today). Let strategy be
  'smart' | 'off' | 'aggressive' | (fn). Infinite extensibility, zero classes,
  fully tree-shakeable — advanced users plug in matchers we never imagined.
  - Builders stay optional. If plain objects feel clunky, we add tiny
  tree-shakeable field(...) sugar later — but the core eats data, so sugar is
  never required (no framework lock-in). That's the valibot discipline: sugar
  over data, not a DSL you must adopt.

  The one thing worth a real decision: the merge/rank policy

  penalty is a band-aid for "combine per-field scores." The general form is a
  merge function: default min across fields, override for weighted/priority
  ranking. That's the genuinely composable knob (and it subsumes penalty).
  Question is whether v1.0 exposes rank?: (fieldScores) => number or keeps
  penalty as the 90% shorthand.

  So, three things to lock:
  1. 2nd-arg shape — getText fn | fieldSpec[] overload (no options bag), or keep
  a slim options object?
  2. Strategy — allow a custom matcher function alongside the string literals?
  (I'd say yes — it's the whole "components" payoff.)
  3. Merge — penalty shorthand, a general rank function, or both?

  My lean: overloaded 2nd arg, yes to functional strategies, keep penalty as the
  shorthand and allow a rank fn for power users. Where do you land? Once these
  are pinned I'll write the v1.0 plan.

✻ Churned for 1m 43s

※ recap: Building mikrofuzz toward a v1.0 with a redesigned, break-everything API: a small primitive plus composition instead of a fat options bag. Next: you decide three things (2nd-arg shape, functional strategies, penalty vs rank) so I can write the v1.0 plan.

❯ What would rank vs penalty look like, what would each one offer?              
                                                                                
  SHould we be allowing to search by object field? I didn't know we could even  
  do that 😂                                                                    
                                                                                
  I think 4 is getting a little too complicated.                                

● rank vs penalty — here's each, concretely:

  penalty — a per-field number, added to that field's score, then the item still
  takes the best (min) field:
  createFuzzySearch(posts, [
    { text: p => p.title },
    { text: p => p.body, penalty: SCORES.CONTAINS },   // body's score += 2
  ]);
  // item score = min(titleScore, bodyScore + 2)
  Offers: "push this field down." One number, local, per-field. Nails "body
  never outranks title." Can't weight, prioritize, average, or require-both.

  rank — a function that gets all the per-field results and returns the single
  item score:
  createFuzzySearch(posts, {
    fields: [{ text: p => p.title }, { text: p => p.body }],
    rank: (m) => m.title?.score ?? (m.body ? m.body.score + 2 : Infinity),
  });
  Offers: any merge policy — priority ("title if it hit, else body"), weighting
  (title*0.5 + body), require-both, average. It's the general form, and it
  subsumes penalty (penalty 2 on body ≡ rank: min(title, body+2)).

  The relationship is the whole point: penalty ⊂ rank. penalty is the ergonomic
  shorthand for the one case everyone actually hits; rank is the escape hatch
  for everything else — but it's verbose, the caller juggles nulls, and it's
  less discoverable.

  My rec: penalty only for v1.0. rank is YAGNI right now, and the exotic cases
  are already reachable via the primitive (fuzzyMatch per field + your own
  merge). The one real argument for rank is that the primitive has no
  preprocessing cache, so "custom merge over a cached collection" is the gap
  only rank fills — but that's speculative. Ship penalty; add rank in v1.1 if a
  real need shows up. Keeps the convenience layer to a single knob.

  ---
  Object-field search — yes, it's been there since v0.1 ({ key: 'name' } and
  getText). You didn't notice because the options bag buried it 😄 — which is
  exactly the argument for the redesign. It's a core, standard capability (Fuse,
  match-sorter all do it: search users by name, products by title). Keep it — 
  but surface it as the positional arg:
  createFuzzySearch(users, u => u.name)('john');   // obvious, typed
  And for v1.0 I'd drop the stringly key: 'name' entirely — u => u.name is
  barely longer, fully typed, and has no "key doesn't exist at runtime" footgun.
  One way to extract text, and it's a function.

  ---
  #4 (functional strategy injection) — agreed, cut it. You're right, it's too
  much: it leaks internal contracts (normalized strings, the [score, ranges]
  tuple) onto users for a case almost nobody needs. strategy stays a plain
  string enum ('smart' | 'off' | 'aggressive'). If someone truly needs a custom
  matcher, they use the primitive. One less concept.

  So v1.0 is shaping up as: primitive fuzzyMatch + a thin 
  createFuzzySearch(list, getText?|fieldSpec[]) with strategy/penalty/acronym 
  per field, default min-merge, no options bag, no key, no custom-strategy, no 
  rank. That's a genuinely small, sharp surface. Want me to write that up as the
  v1.0 plan?

  ⎿  Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/validated-seeking-gizmo.md · /plan to edit
     mikrofuzz v1.0.0 — primitive-first API redesign (breaking)

     Context

     The v0.2.0 work (uncommitted on main) fixed the 6 known bugs and added a
     native
     regex perf gate — both keepers — but it also grew a fat createFuzzySearch
     options
     bag (fields/penalty/acronym/scores/key/getText) and parallel matches+
     scores result arrays. That's overload for a 2.5 kB "does one thing"
     library.

     v1.0 rebalances toward the uFuzzy lesson (expose primitives, compose; don't
     grow
     options): a rich single-string primitive plus a thin collection convenience
     built on it. Breaking is intended — this ships as 1.0.0. Design was settled
     interactively; decisions locked below.

     Carried over unchanged: the 6 bug fixes (punctuation boundaries,
     occurrence-
     walking, flat multi-word, empty-query→null, normalized-length widths) and
     the L1
     fuzzy subsequence gate (buildFuzzyGate, MatchQuery).

     Locked decisions

     - Primitive returns { score, tier, ranges } — tier (categorical) answers
     the
     numbers-vs-tier question at the atom; score stays the sort key.
     - No options bag on createFuzzySearch. 2nd arg is a getText fn or a
     field-spec
     array (three overloads). key (stringly property) is dropped.
     - Merge = default min + per-field penalty shorthand only. No rank fn
     (YAGNI;
     exotic merges use the primitive). penalty ⊂ rank.
     - strategy stays a string enum. No custom-matcher-function injection
     (dropped #4 —
     leaks internal contracts).
     - acronym stays as an opt (per-field + primitive), opt-in, default false.
     - Result arrays consolidate: old matches[] + scores[] → one fields: 
     Array<MatchResult|null>.

     Public API (final)

     // ---- types ----
     type Range = [number, number];                 // inclusive
     type HighlightRanges = Range[];
     type Strategy = "off" | "smart" | "aggressive";
     type Tier =
       | "exact" | "normalized-exact" | "prefix" | "boundary-exact"
       | "boundary" | "multi-word" | "acronym" | "contains" | "fuzzy";

     type MatchResult = { score: number; tier: Tier; ranges: HighlightRanges };

     type FieldSpec<T> = {
       text: (item: T) => string | null;
       strategy?: Strategy;   // default "smart"
       acronym?: boolean;     // default false
       penalty?: number;      // added to this field's score; default 0; keep >=
     0
     };

     type FuzzyResult<T> = {
       item: T;
       score: number;                         // min effective score across 
     fields
       fields: Array<MatchResult | null>;     // one per field spec (null = no 
     match)
     };

     type FuzzySearcher<T> = (query: string) => FuzzyResult<T>[];
     // (kept the FuzzyResult/FuzzySearcher names, not bare Result/Searcher, to 
     avoid
     //  clashes on the consumer side — but the SHAPE is new/breaking.)

     // ---- functions ----
     // The primitive: score ONE string. tier + score + ranges. Stateless.
     fuzzyMatch(text: string, query: string, options?: { strategy?: Strategy;
     acronym?: boolean }): MatchResult | null;

     // Collection convenience (preprocessing-cached, sorted). Three overloads:
     createFuzzySearch(list: string[]): FuzzySearcher<string>;
     createFuzzySearch<T>(list: T[], getText: (item: T) => string | null):
     FuzzySearcher<T>;
     createFuzzySearch<T>(list: T[], fields: FieldSpec<T>[]): FuzzySearcher<T>;

     // building blocks
     normalizeText(str: string): string;
     splitWords(str: string): string[];                 // newly exported
     matchDensity(ranges: HighlightRanges): number;      // include; 
     lowest-value, cuttable
     const SCORES: { EXACT; NORMALIZED_EXACT; PREFIX; BOUNDARY_EXACT; BOUNDARY;
     MULTI_WORD; ACRONYM; CONTAINS };

     Notes:
     - Tier names map 1:1 to SCORES keys, plus "fuzzy" (a range, no constant).
     Both ship:
     SCORES for numeric thresholds / the penalty: SCORES.CONTAINS idiom; Tier
     for
     categorical reads (r.fields[0]?.tier === "prefix").
     - MatchResult is reused as the per-field type in Result.fields (score there
     is the
     effective, post-penalty value; tier is the raw match tier).
     - Highlight access: result.fields[i]?.ranges (single-field → fields[0]).

     File changes

     - src/scores.ts: keep SCORES. Add a TIER name mapping if helpful (or derive
     tier
     names inline in match.ts).
     - src/match.ts: matchField returns MatchResult | null (add tier to every
     tier's
     return; fuzzy dispatch wraps matcher output as tier: "fuzzy"). Keep
     boundaryOccurrence,
     acronymMatch, the fuzzy gate use, and MatchQuery.
     - src/fuzzy.ts: unchanged matchers + buildFuzzyGate; still return [score, 
     ranges]
     (match.ts adds the "fuzzy" tier). Keep CHUNK_SCORES.
     - src/search.ts: rewrite createFuzzySearch to the 3 overloads; normalize
     the 2nd arg
     into FieldSpec[] (string[]→identity spec; fn→one spec; array→as given). Per
     query build
     MatchQuery once (gate + tokens). Per item/field: matchField → apply penalty
     to
     .score → push MatchResult|null into fields; item score = min(effective).
     Drop key.
     Rewrite fuzzyMatch to return MatchResult | null (no item/matches/scores);
     add the
     options arg (strategy/acronym); keep empty-query→null.
     - src/normalize.ts: unchanged (normalizeText, splitWords).
     - src/index.ts: export fuzzyMatch, createFuzzySearch, normalizeText,
     splitWords,
     matchDensity, SCORES; export type *. Update header comment to point at
     SCORES/Tier
     instead of restating magic numbers.
     - src/types.ts: replace with the types above (MatchResult, FieldSpec,
     Result,
     Tier, Strategy, drop
     FuzzyResult/FuzzyMatches/FuzzySearchOptions/FuzzySearchField/
     FuzzySearcher — or rename Result→ keep FuzzyResult? use the new names).

     Tests

     The result shape changes everywhere → most test files need updates, not
     just additions.

     - Rewrite assertions: fuzzyMatch(...) now returns { score, tier, ranges }
     (was
     { item, score, matches, scores }); collection results use r.fields[i] (was
     r.matches[i] / r.scores[i]). Update fuzzy-match.test.ts,
     create-fuzzy-search.test.ts,
     strategies.test.ts, scores.test.ts, fields.test.ts, acronym.test.ts,
     known-issues.test.ts.
     - New: tier.test.ts — every tier returns its correct Tier name;
     primitive.test.ts —
     fuzzyMatch options (strategy/acronym) and the {score,tier,ranges} shape.
     - Reframe fields.test.ts to the field-spec-array API + penalty; drop key
     tests.
     - types.test.ts: the 3 overloads infer T; FieldSpec<T>.text typed; no key.
     - Keep density.test.ts, tier-constants.test.ts, normalize.test.ts (add
     splitWords).

     Docs / meta

     - README.md: full rewrite around the primitive + createFuzzySearch
     overloads; Tier +
     SCORES; per-field penalty; building blocks; drop
     key/fields-options/scores/rank.
     - CHANGELOG.md: 1.0.0 — breaking: new result shape ({score,tier,ranges} /
     fields),
     removed key and the options bag, getText returns one string, tier added;
     plus the
     carried bug fixes + perf gate.
     - docs/naming.md: update to the v1.0 vocabulary (MatchResult, FieldSpec,
     Tier, Result).
     - KNOWN-ISSUES.md: keep the "fixed" status.
     - package.json: version → 1.0.0.
     - Bench devDeps (fuse.js/match-sorter/@leeoniya/ufuzzy) +
     bench/compare.bench.ts stay;
     update the bench to the new API.

     Verification

     1. pnpm lint:types → 0 (incl. the 3-overload inference in types.test.ts).
     2. pnpm test → all green; known-issues stays all-pass (the 6 fixes hold
     under the new shape).
     3. pnpm exec oxlint → 0.
     4. pnpm build → succeeds; dist/index.d.ts shows the v1.0 surface
     (MatchResult, Tier,
     Result, FieldSpec, 3 createFuzzySearch overloads, splitWords, no
     key/FuzzyResult).
     5. pnpm bench → confirm the perf gate still holds (~2× over the pre-gate
     baseline).
     6. Smoke: fuzzyMatch("Hello World","wor") →
     {score:1,tier:"boundary",ranges:[[6,8]]};
     createFuzzySearch(users, u=>u.name)("john"); multi-field with penalty: 
     SCORES.CONTAINS
     → body never outranks title, r.fields populated per field with tiers.

     Out of scope (deferred, not deleted)

     - rank merge function (v1.1 if a real weighted/priority need appears — the
     cache gap is the
     only argument for it).
     - Custom-matcher strategy functions.
     - tier on a flattened top-level result (kept per-field in fields).

     Open call

     - matchDensity is the one low-value export — included as a building block,
     but say the word
     and I cut it (one line).

  barrel.

● Write(src/index.ts)
  ⎿  Added 9 lines, removed 13 lines
       2   * Fuzzy search library
       3   * Adapted from @nozbe/microfuzz with Vite SSR compatibility
       4   *
       5 - * Scoring (lower = better):                                   
       6 - * - 0:    Exact match                                         
       7 - * - 0.1:  Case/diacritics-insensitive exact match             
       8 - * - 0.5:  Starts with query                                   
       9 - * - 0.9:  Contains query at word boundary (exact case)        
      10 - * - 1:    Contains query at word boundary                     
      11 - * - 1.5:  Contains all query words (in any order)             
      12 - * - 1.8:  Matches word initials (acronym tier, opt-in)        
      13 - * - 2:    Contains query anywhere                             
      14 - * - 2+:   Fuzzy match (fewer chunks = better)                 
       5 + * Two entry points:                                           
       6 + * - `fuzzyMatch(text, query, options?)` — the primitive: score
         + one string,                                                   
       7 + *   returning `{ score, tier, ranges }`.                      
       8 + * - `createFuzzySearch(list, getText? | fields?)` — a cached, 
         +sorted search over                                             
       9 + *   a collection.                                             
      10   *
      16 - * Per-field `penalty` is added to a field's score (higher demo
         -tes it).                                                       
      11 + * Scoring is lower = better; see the `SCORES` constants and th
         +e `Tier` type.                                                 
      12 + * Any score greater than `SCORES.CONTAINS` is tier "fuzzy".   
      13   */
      14  
      15  export { createFuzzySearch, fuzzyMatch } from "./search";
      20 -export { normalizeText } from "./normalize";                   
      21 -export { SCORES } from "./scores";

      18 +export { SCORES } from "./scores";

       50  
       73 -Lower scores indicate better matches. Import `SCORES` to filte

       74 -tier instead of hardcoding numbers:                           
       51 +Lower is better. Each match reports a numeric `score` (for sor
          +ting) and a categorical `tier`:                               
       52  
       76 -| Score | Constant | Match Type |                             
       77 -|-------|----------|------------|                             
       78 -| 0 | `SCORES.EXACT` | Exact match |                          
       79 -| 0.1 | `SCORES.NORMALIZED_EXACT` | Case/diacritics-insensitiv
          -e exact match |                                               
       80 -| 0.5 | `SCORES.PREFIX` | Starts with query |                 
       81 -| 0.9 | `SCORES.BOUNDARY_EXACT` | Contains at word boundary (e
          -xact case) |                                                  
       82 -| 1 | `SCORES.BOUNDARY` | Contains at word boundary |         
       83 -| 1.5 | `SCORES.MULTI_WORD` | Contains all query words (any or
          -der) |                                                        
       84 -| 1.8 | `SCORES.ACRONYM` | Matches word initials (opt-in, see 
          -`acronym`) |                                                  
       85 -| 2 | `SCORES.CONTAINS` | Contains query anywhere |           
       86 -| 2+ | — | Fuzzy match (fewer chunks = better) |              
       53 +| score | tier | meaning |                                    
       54 +|-------|------|---------|                                    
       55 +| 0 | `exact` | exact match |                                 
       56 +| 0.1 | `normalized-exact` | case / diacritics-insensitive exa
          +ct |                                                          
       57 +| 0.5 | `prefix` | starts with query |                        
       58 +| 0.9 | `boundary-exact` | at a word boundary, exact case |   
       59 +| 1 | `boundary` | at a word boundary |                       
       60 +| 1.5 | `multi-word` | all query words present, any order |   
       61 +| 1.8 | `acronym` | word initials (opt-in via `acronym: true`)
          + |                                                            
       62 +| 2 | `contains` | contains query anywhere |                  
       63 +| > 2 | `fuzzy` | fuzzy chain (fewer chunks = better) |       
       64  
       88 -Any score greater than `SCORES.CONTAINS` is a fuzzy-fallback m

      131 -## API Reference                                              
      132 -                                                              
      133 -### `createFuzzySearch<T>(collection, options?)`              
      134 -                                                              
      135 -Creates a reusable search function for a collection.          
      136 -                                                              
      137 -**Options:**                                                  
      138 -- `key?: string` — Property name to search (for object arrays)
      139 -- `getText?: (item: T) => Array<string | null>` — Custom text 
          -extraction (typed to `T`)                                     
      140 -- `strategy?: "smart" | "aggressive" | "off"` — Matching strat
          -egy                                                           
      141 -- `acronym?: boolean` — Enable the word-initials tier (default
          - `false`)                                                     
      142 -- `fields?: FuzzySearchField<T>[]` — Per-field config (superse
          -des the above)                                                
      143 -                                                              
      144 -**Returns:** `(query: string) => FuzzyResult<T>[]`            
      145 -                                                              
      146 -### `fuzzyMatch(text, query)`                                 
      147 -                                                              
      148 -One-off fuzzy match for a single string. **Returns:** `FuzzyRe
          -sult<string> | null`.                                         
      149 -                                                              
      150 -### `normalizeText(str)`                                      
      151 -                                                              
      152 -Normalize text (lowercase, remove diacritics).                
      153 -                                                              
      154 -### `matchDensity(ranges)`                                    
      155 -                                                              
      156 -Matched characters ÷ inclusive span for one field's `Highlight
          -Ranges` (1 = a single                                         
      157 -solid run; lower = more scattered). A cheap discriminator for 
          -junk fuzzy chains.                                            
      158 -                                                              
      159 -### `SCORES`                                                  
      160 -                                                              
      161 -Frozen object of the tier scores in the Scoring table above.  
      162 -

  uFuzzy, ~4.9× under Fuse. It grew a hair from v0.2 (2.52 → 2.63 kB) — the tier
  strings ("boundary-exact" etc.) and the extra overload/export. +0.11 kB for
  the tier categorical is a good trade.

  Verdict: v1.0 is the fastest and the smallest-vs-peers it's been — ~0.16
  ms/query at 2k, sub-ms through 10k, 2.63 kB, zero deps. Still ~3.75× behind

  a bug.

  hint (node >=18) if you want to signal support. Neither matters much.

  But the build now crashes:
  rollup-plugin-dts .../typescript@7.0.2/...:
  TypeError: Cannot read properties of undefined (reading
  'useCaseSensitiveFileNames')
      ts.sys.useCaseSensitiveFileNames ...
  Why: TypeScript 7 is the brand-new native (Go) compiler — its JS programmatic
  API differs (ts.sys isn't exposed the way rollup-plugin-dts@6.4.1 expects).
  tsc --noEmit (lint:types) works because that's the CLI, but unbuild's .d.ts
  generation goes through the TS API and dies. The build toolchain (unbuild →
  rollup-plugin-dts) simply doesn't support TS7 yet — it's days old, and you're
  on Node 26 too.

  dist/ is still the good v1.0 output from the last successful build (the smoke
  test used it), so nothing's corrupted — but the build isn't reproducible, so
  CI/publish would fail as-is.

  The bump was intentional, so I won't revert without your say-so:

● User answered Claude's questions:
  ⎿  · typescript ^7.0.2 breaks the build (unbuild/rollup-plugin-dts can't run 
     under TS7). How do you want to handle it? → Taking a look at

     Maintenance Mode

     This project is in maintenance mode. That means there will be no more 
     active feature development. There will still be occasional releases to 
     maintain compatibility with future TypeScript releases. Pull Requests are 
     always welcome, however reaction time on both Issues and PRs can be slow.
     What to expect

     While this plugin is fairly complete, it does not support all imaginable 
     use-cases. In particular, the plugin works best with already existing .d.ts
     files generated by the typescript compiler from idiomatic code.

     Working with .ts(x) or even .js(x) (when setting allowJs: true) does work, 
     but is not recommended.

     The plugin does its own import resolution through the typescript compiler, 
     and usage together with other resolution plugins, such as node-resolve can 
     lead to errors and is not recommended.

     All external dependencies from node_modules are automatically excluded from
     bundling. This can be overridden using the respectExternal setting, but it
     is generally not recommended. While rollup of external @types generally 
     works, it is not recommended.
     TS2742 and shared declaration chunks

     When a bundled entry exposes a type that originally came from a private 
     shared chunk, downstream tsc --declaration runs can fail with TS2742.

     This is part of a broader TypeScript declaration portability problem. For 
     upstream context, see ./*.d.ts required in exports to avoid ...not 
     portable... for one shape of the bug, and Elaborate on non-portable types 
     for the related error-message discussion.

     This plugin will try to rewrite that path through an entry that already 
     re-exports the type publicly. That keeps the existing public API and can 
     make the bundled declarations portable for downstream consumers.

     The plugin does not invent new public exports. If no public entry 
     re-exports the shared type, the bundled package can still trigger TS2742. 
     In that case, the plugin emits a warning and the package should re-export 
     the type from a public entry explicitly.
     Why?

     Well, ideally TypeScript should just do all this itself, and it even has a 
     proposal to do that. But there hasn’t been any progress in ~3 years.

     Some projects, like rollup itself go the route of completely separating 
     their public interfaces in a separate file.


     What are our optiosn doing this while not being stuck in the past?

● Smart — rollup-plugin-dts being in maintenance mode is exactly why the TS7
  break is a "stuck in the past" symptom, not a one-off. Let me research the
  modern options rather than guess: test whether TS7's own tsc can emit
  declarations (the cheap escape), and check the current state of the bundlers
  that don't depend on rollup-plugin-dts.

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

  ⎿  Did 1 search in 11s

● The search nailed it — and it points straight at a modern answer. Let me
  verify one thing: whether our code is already isolatedDeclarations-clean (that
  determines if the best option is turnkey).

  Ran 1 shell command (ctrl+o to expand)

● Verified — and the modern path is turnkey. Our src/ is already 
  isolatedDeclarations-clean (no errors, all d.ts emitted — because we gave
  every export an explicit type during the redesign). That unlocks the best
  option.

  Why this keeps happening

  The break isn't really "TS7" — it's that unbuild generates .d.ts through
  rollup-plugin-dts, which drives the TypeScript compiler API. That plugin is in
  maintenance mode, and any tool that couples .d.ts generation to the TS
  compiler API will break again on the next TS shift. The fix is to decouple 
  .d.ts from the TS version.

  Options (not stuck in the past)

  1 — Migrate unbuild → tsdown, generate .d.ts via oxc isolatedDeclarations. ⭐ 
  Recommended.
  tsdown is the rolldown-based library bundler from the Vite/oxc team (the
  tsup/unbuild successor). With isolatedDeclarations: true, it emits
  declarations with oxc-transform — from syntax, no tsc, no rollup-plugin-dts.
  That means:
  - The build no longer depends on the TypeScript version at all — TS5, TS7,
  tsgo, whatever. The break vanishes and can't recur.
  - ~7× faster .d.ts generation (tsdown docs).
  - Consolidates on the oxc stack you already run (oxlint, oxfmt).
  - Drops maintenance-mode rollup-plugin-dts for the actively-maintained
  rolldown-plugin-dts.
  - Turnkey — src is already iso-clean, so zero code changes. Bonus guardrail:
  oxc forces every export to keep an explicit type (or it errors), which is good
  hygiene for a public API.
  - Output shape is unchanged (bundled dist/index.d.ts + index.mjs), so
  exports/types stay as-is.

  2 — tsdown with the tsgo generator (keep TS7). tsdown auto-uses TS7's native
  tsgo for d.ts. Works, but tsdown flags tsgo as experimental, not for 
  production — and it's still TS-version-coupled. The oxc path (option 1) is
  strictly better.

  3 — Revert TS to 5.x, stay on unbuild. The boring stopgap. Works today, but
  keeps you on maintenance-mode rollup-plugin-dts and undoes the upgrade — i.e.
  literally "stuck in the past." Fine only as a temporary unblock.

  4 — Hand-assemble (tsgo emitDeclarationOnly + esbuild/rolldown for JS). More
  moving parts than tsdown packages for you. Not worth it.

  Recommendation

  Option 1. It fixes the immediate TS7 break, makes the build immune to future 
  TS-version churn (the real disease, not just this symptom), speeds it up ~7×,
  and lands on the same oxc toolchain you've already committed to — with no
  source changes needed.

  Want me to do the migration now? It's: add tsdown (drop unbuild), a small
  tsdown.config.ts, isolatedDeclarations: true in tsconfig, point build at
  tsdown — then verify the d.ts + dist come out identical and re-run the full
  gate.

✻ Churned for 7m 28s

❯ Tsdown vs using vite?                                                         

● Different tools for different jobs. Short version: Vite is for apps, tsdown is
  for libraries — and for a library, Vite doesn't even solve the problem we're 
  fixing.

  ┌──────────┬──────────────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────┐
  │          │              tsdown              │    Vite (library mode)    │
  ├──────────┼──────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────┤
  │ Built    │ libraries (packages)             │ apps (dev server, HMR);   │
  │ for      │                                  │ lib mode is a bolt-on     │
  ├──────────┼──────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────┤
  │ Engine   │ Rolldown (Rust)                  │ Rollup (JS)               │
  ├──────────┼──────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────┤
  │          │ oxc / isolatedDeclarations —     │ needs vite-plugin-dts →   │
  │ .d.ts    │ TS-version-independent           │ the TS compiler API /     │
  │          │                                  │ api-extractor             │
  ├──────────┼──────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────┤
  │ Config   │ minimal, package-shaped          │ build.lib + rollupOptions │
  │          │ (entry/format/dts/exports)       │  externals + dts plugin   │
  ├──────────┼──────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────┤
  │ Dev      │                                  │                           │
  │ server / │ no (not its job)                 │ yes                       │
  │  HMR     │                                  │                           │
  └──────────┴──────────────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────┘

  The decisive point: Vite's build is Rollup, and to emit types for a TS library
  you add vite-plugin-dts, which drives the TypeScript compiler (plus
  api-extractor for bundling). That's the same TS-compiler coupling that just
  broke us on TS7. So Vite lib mode would reintroduce the exact disease — it
  doesn't decouple .d.ts from the TS version. tsdown's oxc/isolatedDeclarations
  path is what actually cures it. (And you can't easily bolt rolldown-plugin-dts
  onto Vite yet — Vite still runs Rollup, not Rolldown.)

  Other reasons tsdown fits here:
  - For a 2.6 kB zero-dep package you don't need a dev server, HMR, or the app
  plugin surface — Vite is overkill.
  - tsdown is the Vite team's answer for libraries (Rolldown is Vite's future
  engine; they point library authors at tsdown). It's not "Vite vs a rival" —
  it's the library-shaped sibling.
  - Less config, fewer plugins to keep current.

  When Vite would make sense: if this repo also wanted a demo/playground app or 
  dev server alongside the library — then one Vite setup could serve both, and
  you'd accept vite-plugin-dts for types. mikrofuzz is a pure library with no
  app, so that doesn't apply.

  Verdict unchanged: tsdown. It's purpose-built for this, kills the TS-version
  coupling for good, is ~7× faster on d.ts, and rides the oxc stack you already
  use. Vite would be a heavier setup that leaves the root cause in place.

  Want me to go ahead with the tsdown migration (add tsdown, drop unbuild,
  isolatedDeclarations: true, small tsdown.config.ts), then verify dist comes
  out identical and run the full gate?

  (match-sorter 4.1, uFuzzy 8.7, Fuse 12.8). Great selling point.
  - Speed: relative, not absolute. I'd avoid pinning exact hz/ms in the README —
  they're machine-specific (measured here on Node 26) and rot fast, and readers
  will run different hardware. Better: "sub-millisecond per query for lists up
  to ~10k short items; faster than match-sorter, ~3× behind uFuzzy (a
  native-regex engine); no typo tolerance (use Fuse for that)." Honest
  positioning that won't go stale.
  - Tighten the tagline 2.5 → 2.4 kB.

  honest caveats), plus a bench:json script for machine-readable output. Want
  both? And should the speed be the relative framing (recommended) or do you
  actually want the absolute numbers in there?

※ recap: mikrofuzz v1.0.0 is built, tested, and committed on branch v1 (3 commits, clean, all green). Next: merge v1 into main and tag v1.0.0 to publish, on your go-ahead. (disable recaps in /config)

❯ Do we need a migrate doc for beta to v1?                                      

● Honest answer: not strictly needed — the CHANGELOG's "Breaking" section
  already lists the what, and 0.1.0's adoption is probably small. But a v1.0
  with real API breaks deserves a short before/after guide, and it's cheap
  because the breaking surface is tiny (~4 changes). So: worth it, kept concise.

  Here's the whole migration — it fits in a handful of snippets:

  // 1. fuzzyMatch result shape
  - const { item, score, matches } = fuzzyMatch(text, q);  // matches: [[[6,8]]]
  + const { score, tier, ranges } = fuzzyMatch(text, q);   // ranges: [[6,8]], +
  tier

  // 2. search objects by property — `key` is gone
  - createFuzzySearch(users, { key: "name" });
  + createFuzzySearch(users, (u) => u.name);

  // 3. multi-field — getText array → field specs
  - createFuzzySearch(users, { getText: (u) => [u.name, u.email] });
  + createFuzzySearch(users, [{ text: (u) => u.name }, { text: (u) => u.email
  }]);

  // 4. result: matches[] / scores[] → one fields[]
  - result.matches[i];          // HighlightRanges | null
  + result.fields[i]?.ranges;   // + .tier, .score

  Plus a note that strategy moved onto the primitive options / per-field spec,
  and tier/splitWords/matchDensity/SCORES are new.

  That's the entire thing — small enough that it's low-cost polish, not a chore.

  Recommendation: a short MIGRATION.md (linked from the CHANGELOG and README),
  rather than bloating the README — it keeps the main doc focused and gives a
  clean landing spot for "upgrading from 0.x".

  Want me to write it? And MIGRATION.md as a separate file, or a ## Migrating 
  from 0.x section in the README?
